<tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1999_NJ_Proof.png" title="New Jersey quarter dollar coin">\n          <img alt="New Jersey quarter dollar coin" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="772" height="85" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/1999_NJ_Proof.png/85px-1999_NJ_Proof.png" States state symbols">\n          Lists of United States state symbols\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        New Jersey\n       </b>\n       is a\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">\n        state\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">\n        Northeastern\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_States" title="Mid-Atlantic States">\n        mid-Atlantic\n       </a>\n       regions of the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       . It is a\n       <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">\n        peninsula\n       </a>\n       , bordered on the north and east by the state of\n       <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">\n        New York\n       </a>\n       ; on the east, southeast, and south by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">\n        Atlantic Ocean\n       </a>\n       ; on the west by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River" title="Delaware River">\n        Delaware River\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">\n        Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       ; and on the southwest by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Bay" title="Delaware Bay">\n        Delaware Bay\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">\n        Delaware\n       </a>\n       . New Jersey is the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_area" title="List of U.S. states and territories by area">\n        fourth-smallest state\n       </a>\n       by area but the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population">\n        11th-most populous\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population_density" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population density">\n        most densely populated\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states" title="List of U.S. states">\n        50 U.S. states\n       </a>\n       . New Jersey lies entirely within the\n       <a href="/wiki/Combined_statistical_area" title="Combined statistical area">\n        combined statistical areas\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">\n        New York City\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">\n        Philadelphia\n       </a>\n       and is the third-wealthiest state by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Median_household_income" title="Median household income">\n        median household income\n       </a>\n       as of 2016.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NJMedianIncome_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NJMedianIncome-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey was inhabited by\n       <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">\n        Native Americans\n       </a>\n       for more than 2,800 years, with historical tribes such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lenape" title="Lenape">\n        Lenape\n       </a>\n       along the coast. In the early 17th century, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">\n        Dutch\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">\n        Swedes\n       </a>\n       made the first European settlements in the state.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">\n        English\n       </a>\n       later seized control of the region,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       naming it the\n       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_New_Jersey" title="Province of New Jersey">\n        Province of New Jersey\n       </a>\n       after the largest of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">\n        Channel Islands\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">\n        Jersey\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and granting it as a colony to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_George_Carteret" title="Sir George Carteret">\n        Sir George Carteret\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Berkeley,_1st_Baron_Berkeley_of_Stratton" title="John Berkeley, 1st Baron Berkeley of Stratton">\n        John Berkeley, 1st Baron Berkeley of Stratton\n       </a>\n       . New Jersey was the site of several decisive battles during the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">\n        American Revolutionary War\n       </a>\n       in the 18th century.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the 19th century, factories in cities (known as the "Big Six"\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/Camden,_New_Jersey" title="Camden, New Jersey">\n        Camden\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Paterson,_New_Jersey" title="Paterson, New Jersey">\n        Paterson\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey" title="Newark, New Jersey">\n        Newark\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Trenton,_New_Jersey" title="Trenton, New Jersey">\n        Trenton\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jersey_City,_New_Jersey" title="Jersey City, New Jersey">\n        Jersey City\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth,_New_Jersey" title="Elizabeth, New Jersey">\n        Elizabeth\n       </a>\n       helped to drive the\n       <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">\n        Industrial Revolution\n       </a>\n       . New Jersey\'s geographic location at the center of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northeast_megalopolis" title="Northeast megalopolis">\n        Northeast megalopolis\n       </a>\n       , between\n       <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">\n        Boston\n       </a>\n       and New York City to the northeast, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">\n        Philadelphia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">\n        Baltimore\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">\n        Washington, D.C.\n       </a>\n       , to the southwest, fueled its rapid growth through the process of\n       <a href="/wiki/Suburbanization" title="Suburbanization">\n        suburbanization\n       </a>\n       in the second half of the 20th century. In the first decades of the\n       <a href="/wiki/21st_century" title="21st century">\n        21st century\n       </a>\n       , this suburbanization began reverting with the consolidation of New Jersey\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_enclave" title="Ethnic enclave">\n        culturally diverse\n       </a>\n       populace toward more urban settings within the state,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReUrbanizationNJ2_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ReUrbanizationNJ2-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReUrbanizationNJ_26-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ReUrbanizationNJ-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       with towns home to\n       <a href="/wiki/Commuter_rail_in_North_America" title="Commuter rail in North America">\n        commuter rail stations\n       </a>\n       outpacing the population growth of more\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automobile" title="Automobile">\n        automobile\n       </a>\n       -oriented suburbs since 2008.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#History">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           1\n          </span>\n      Notable people\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-63">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           13\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-64">\n         <a   <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_Jersey" title="History of New Jersey">\n        History of New Jersey\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Around 180 million years ago, during the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jurassic_Period" title="Jurassic Period">\n        Jurassic Period\n       </a>\n       , New Jersey bordered North Africa. The pressure of the collision between North America and Africa gave rise to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">\n        Appalachian Mountains\n       </a>\n       . Around 18,000 years ago, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_glaciation" title="Wisconsin glaciation">\n        Ice Age\n       </a>\n       resulted in\n       <a href="/wiki/Glacier" title="Glacier">\n        glaciers\n       </a>\n       that reached New Jersey. As the glaciers retreated, they left behind\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glacial_Lake_Passaic" title="Glacial Lake Passaic">\n        Lake Passaic\n       </a>\n       , as well as many rivers, swamps, and gorges.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey was originally settled by Native Americans, with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lenape" title="Lenape">\n        Lenni-Lenape\n       </a>\n       being dominant at the time of contact.\n       <i>\n        Scheyichbi\n       </i>\n       is the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lenape_language" title="Lenape language">\n        Lenape\n       </a>\n       name for the land that is now New Jersey.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Lenape were several\n       <a href="/wiki/Autonomy" title="Autonomy">\n        autonomous\n       </a>\n       groups that practiced\n       <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">\n        maize\n       </a>\n       agriculture in order to supplement their hunting and gathering in the region surrounding the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River" title="Delaware River">\n        Delaware River\n       </a>\n       , the lower\n       <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">\n        Hudson River\n       </a>\n       , and western\n       <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_Sound" title="Long Island Sound">\n        Long Island Sound\n       </a>\n       . The Lenape society was divided into\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matrilinear" title="Matrilinear">\n        matrilinear\n       </a>\n       clans that were based upon common female ancestors. These clans were organized into three distinct\n       <a href="/wiki/Phratry" title="Phratry">\n        phratries\n       </a>\n       identified by their animal sign:\n       <a href="/wiki/Turtle" title="Turtle">\n        Turtle\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Turkey_(bird)" title="Turkey (bird)">\n        Turkey\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wolf" title="Wolf">\n        Wolf\n       </a>\n       . They first encountered the Dutch in the early 17th century, and their primary relationship with the Europeans was through\n       <a href="/wiki/Fur_trade" title="Fur trade">\n        fur trade\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_era">\n        Colonial era\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Colonial_history_of_New_Jersey" title="Colonial history of New Jersey">\n        Colonial history of New Jersey\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nieuw_Nederland_and_Nya_Sverige.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1215" data-file-width="835" height="247" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Nieuw_Nederland_and_Nya_Sverige.svg/170px-Nieuw_Nederland_and_Nya_Sverige.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Nieuw_Nederland_and_Nya_Sverige.svg/255px-Nieuw_Nederland_and_Nya_Sverige.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Nieuw_Nederland_and_Nya_Sverige.svg/340px-Nieuw_Nederland_and_Nya_Sverige.svg.png 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nieuw_Nederland_and_Nya_Sverige.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The relative location of the New Netherland and New Sweden settlements in eastern North America\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">\n        Dutch\n       </a>\n       became the first Europeans to lay claim to lands in New Jersey. The Dutch colony of\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">\n        New Netherland\n       </a>\n       consisted of parts of modern\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle_Atlantic" title="Middle Atlantic">\n        Middle Atlantic\n       </a>\n       states. Although the European principle of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Land_ownership" title="Land ownership">\n        land ownership\n       </a>\n       was not recognized by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lenape" title="Lenape">\n        Lenape\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">\n        Dutch West India Company\n       </a>\n       policy required its colonists to purchase the land that they settled. The first to do so was\n       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Reyniersz_Pauw" title="Michael Reyniersz Pauw">\n        Michiel Pauw\n       </a>\n       who established a patronship called\n       <a href="/wiki/Pavonia,_New_Netherland" title="Pavonia, New Netherland">\n        Pavonia\n       </a>\n       in 1630 along the\n       <a href="/wiki/North_River_(Hudson_River)" title="North River (Hudson River)">\n        North River\n       </a>\n       which eventually became the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bergen,_New_Netherland" title="Bergen, New Netherland">\n        Bergen\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Minuit" title="Peter Minuit">\n        Peter Minuit\n       </a>\n       \'s purchase of lands along the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River" title="Delaware River">\n        Delaware River\n       </a>\n       established the colony of\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Sweden" title="New Sweden">\n        New Sweden\n       </a>\n       . The entire region became a territory of\n       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">\n        England\n       </a>\n       on June 24, 1664, after an English fleet under the command of Colonel\n       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nicolls" title="Richard Nicolls">\n        Richard Nicolls\n       </a>\n       sailed into what is today\n       <a href="/wiki/New_York_Harbor" title="New York Harbor">\n        New York Harbor\n       </a>\n       and took control of\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Amsterdam" title="Fort Amsterdam">\n        Fort Amsterdam\n       </a>\n       , annexing the entire province.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the\n       <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">\n        English Civil War\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">\n        Channel Island\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">\n        Jersey\n       </a>\n       remained loyal to the British Crown and gave sanctuary to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_England" title="King of England">\n        King\n       </a>\n       . It was from the Royal Square in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Helier" title="St. Helier">\n        St. Helier\n       </a>\n       that\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">\n        Charles II of England\n       </a>\n       was proclaimed King in 1649, following the execution of his father,\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">\n        Charles I\n       </a>\n       . The North American lands were divided by\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">\n        Charles II\n       </a>\n       , who gave his brother, the Duke of York (later\n       <a href="/wiki/James_II_of_England" title="James II of England">\n        King James II\n       </a>\n       ), the region between\n       <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">\n        New England\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">\n        Maryland\n       </a>\n       as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_colony" title="Proprietary colony">\n        proprietary colony\n       </a>\n       (as opposed to a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_colony" title="Royal colony">\n        royal colony\n       </a>\n       ). James then granted the land between the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">\n        Hudson River\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River" title="Delaware River">\n        Delaware River\n       </a>\n       (the land that would become New Jersey) to two friends who had remained loyal through the\n       <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">\n        English Civil War\n       </a>\n       :\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Carteret" title="George Carteret">\n        Sir George Carteret\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Berkeley,_1st_Baron_Berkeley_of_Stratton" title="John Berkeley, 1st Baron Berkeley of Stratton">\n        Lord Berkeley of Stratton\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The area was named the\n       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_New_Jersey" title="Province of New Jersey">\n        Province of New Jersey\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Since the state\'s inception, New Jersey has been characterized by\n       <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">\n        ethnic and religious diversity\n       </a>\n       . New England\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congregationalists" title="Congregationalists">\n        Congregationalists\n       </a>\n       settled alongside\n       <a href="/wiki/Scots%27_Church,_Melbourne" title="Scots\' Church, Melbourne">\n        Scots Presbyterians\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_Reformed" title="Dutch Reformed">\n        Dutch Reformed\n       </a>\n       migrants. While the majority of residents lived in towns with individual landholdings of 100 acres (40\xc2\xa0ha), a few rich proprietors owned vast estates. English\n       <a href="/wiki/Quakers" title="Quakers">\n        Quakers\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglicans" title="Anglicans">\n        Anglicans\n       </a>\n       owned large landholdings. Unlike\n       <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Colony" title="Plymouth Colony">\n        Plymouth Colony\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">\n        Jamestown\n       </a>\n       and other colonies, New Jersey was populated by a secondary wave of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigrants" title="Immigrants">\n        immigrants\n       </a>\n       who came from other colonies instead of those who migrated directly from Europe. New Jersey remained agrarian and rural throughout the colonial era, and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commercial_agriculture" title="Commercial agriculture">\n        commercial farming\n       </a>\n       developed sporadically. Some townships, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Burlington,_New_Jersey" title="Burlington, New Jersey">\n        Burlington\n       </a>\n       on the Delaware River and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Perth_Amboy" title="Perth Amboy">\n        Perth Amboy\n       </a>\n       , emerged as important\n       <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">\n        ports\n       </a>\n       for shipping to New York City and Philadelphia. The colony\'s fertile lands and tolerant religious policy drew more settlers, and New Jersey\'s population had increased to 120,000 by 1775.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Settlement for the first 10 years of English rule took place along\n       <a href="/wiki/Hackensack_River" title="Hackensack River">\n        Hackensack River\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Kill" title="Arthur Kill">\n        Arthur Kill\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 settlers came primarily from New York and New England. On March 18, 1673, Berkeley sold his half of the colony to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Religious_Society_of_Friends" title="Religious Society of Friends">\n        Quakers\n       </a>\n       in England, who settled the Delaware Valley region as a Quaker colony. (\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Penn" title="William Penn">\n        William Penn\n       </a>\n       acted as trustee for the lands for a time.) New Jersey was governed very briefly as two distinct provinces,\n       <a href="/wiki/East_Jersey" title="East Jersey">\n        East\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Jersey" title="West Jersey">\n        West Jersey\n       </a>\n       , for 28 years between 1674 and 1702, at times part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_New_York" title="Province of New York">\n        Province of New York\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_New_England" title="Dominion of New England">\n        Dominion of New England\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1702, the two provinces were reunited under a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Governor_of_New_Jersey" title="Royal Governor of New Jersey">\n        royal governor\n       </a>\n       , rather than a\n       <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_governor" title="Proprietary governor">\n        proprietary one\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Edward_Hyde,_3rd_Earl_of_Clarendon" title="Edward Hyde, 3rd Earl of Clarendon">\n        Edward Hyde\n       </a>\n       , Lord Cornbury, became the first governor of the colony as a royal colony. Britain believed that he was an ineffective and corrupt ruler, taking bribes and speculating on land. In 1708 he was recalled to England. New Jersey was then ruled by the governors of New York, but this infuriated the settlers of New Jersey, who accused those governors of favoritism to New York.\n       <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Morris_(governor)" title="Lewis Morris (governor)">\n        Judge Lewis Morris\n       </a>\n       led the case for a separate governor, and was appointed governor by\n       <a href="/wiki/George_II_of_Great_Britain" title="George II of Great Britain">\n        King George II\n       </a>\n       in 1738.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Revolutionary_War_era">\n        Revolutionary War era\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_in_the_American_Revolution" title="New Jersey in the American Revolution">\n        New Jersey in the American Revolution\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey was one of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">\n        Thirteen Colonies\n       </a>\n       that revolted against British rule in the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">\n        American Revolution\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/New_Jersey_Constitution_of_1776" title="s:New Jersey Constitution of 1776">\n        New Jersey Constitution of 1776\n       </a>\n       was passed July 2, 1776, just two days before the\n       <a href="/wiki/Second_Continental_Congress" title="Second Continental Congress">\n        Second Continental Congress\n       </a>\n       declared American Independence from\n       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">\n        Great Britain\n       </a>\n       . It was an act of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Provincial_Congress_of_New_Jersey" title="Provincial Congress of New Jersey">\n        Provincial Congress\n       </a>\n       , which made itself into the state Legislature. To reassure neutrals, it provided that it would become void if New Jersey reached reconciliation with Great Britain.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey representatives\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richard_Stockton_(1730%E2%80%931781)" title="Richard Stockton (1730\xe2\x80\x931781)">\n        Richard Stockton\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Witherspoon" title="John Witherspoon">\n        John Witherspoon\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Francis_Hopkinson" title="Francis Hopkinson">\n        Francis Hopkinson\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Hart_(New_Jersey_politician)" title="John Hart (New Jersey politician)">\n        John Hart\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Clark" title="Abraham Clark">\n        Abraham Clark\n       </a>\n       were among those who signed the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">\n        United States Declaration of Independence\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_by_Emanuel_Leutze,_MMA-NYC,_1851.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3847" data-file-width="6004" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_by_Emanuel_Leutze%2C_MMA-NYC%2C_1851.jpg/220px-Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_by_Emanuel_Leutze%2C_MMA-NYC%2C_1851.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_by_Emanuel_Leutze%2C_MMA-NYC%2C_1851.jpg/330px-Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_by_Emanuel_Leutze%2C_MMA-NYC%2C_1851.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_by_Emanuel_Leutze%2C_MMA-NYC%2C_1851.jpg/440px-Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_by_Emanuel_Leutze%2C_MMA-NYC%2C_1851.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_by_Emanuel_Leutze,_MMA-NYC,_1851.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware" title="Washington Crossing the Delaware">\n           Washington Crossing the Delaware\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         during the\n         <a href="/wiki/New_York_and_New_Jersey_campaign" title="New York and New Jersey campaign">\n          New York and New Jersey campaign\n         </a>\n         , winter 1777\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       During the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">\n        American Revolutionary War\n       </a>\n       , British and American armies crossed New Jersey numerous times, and several pivotal battles took place in the state. Because of this, New Jersey today is often referred to as "The Crossroads of the American Revolution."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The winter quarters of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Continental_Army" title="Continental Army">\n        Continental Army\n       </a>\n       were established there twice by General\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">\n        George Washington\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Morristown,_New_Jersey" title="Morristown, New Jersey">\n        Morristown\n       </a>\n       , which has been called "The Military Capital of the American Revolution".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Princetonwashington.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3099" data-file-width="4143" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Princetonwashington.jpg/220px-Princetonwashington.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Princetonwashington.jpg/330px-Princetonwashington.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Princetonwashington.jpg/440px-Princetonwashington.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Princetonwashington.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">\n          George Washington\n         </a>\n         rallying his troops at the\n         <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Princeton" title="Battle of Princeton">\n          Battle of Princeton\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       On the night of December\xc2\xa025\xe2\x80\x9326, 1776, the Continental Army under\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington%27s_crossing_of_the_Delaware_River" title="Washington\'s crossing of the Delaware River">\n        George Washington crossed the Delaware River\n       </a>\n       . After the crossing, he surprised and defeated the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hessian_(soldiers)" title="Hessian (soldiers)">\n        Hessian troops\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trenton" title="Battle of Trenton">\n        Battle of Trenton\n       </a>\n       . Slightly more than a week after victory at\n       <a href="/wiki/Trenton,_New_Jersey" title="Trenton, New Jersey">\n        Trenton\n       </a>\n       , American forces gained an important victory by stopping\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Cornwallis,_1st_Marquess_Cornwallis" title="Charles Cornwallis, 1st Marquess Cornwallis">\n        General Cornwallis\'s\n       </a>\n       charges at the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Trenton" title="Second Battle of Trenton">\n        Second Battle of Trenton\n       </a>\n       . By evading Cornwallis\'s army, Washington made a surprise attack on\n       <a href="/wiki/Princeton,_New_Jersey" title="Princeton, New Jersey">\n        Princeton\n       </a>\n       and successfully defeated the British forces there on January 3, 1777.\n       <a href="/wiki/Emanuel_Leutze" title="Emanuel Leutze">\n        Emanuel Leutze\n       </a>\n       \'s painting of\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware" title="Washington Crossing the Delaware">\n         Washington Crossing the Delaware\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       became an icon of the Revolution.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       American forces under Washington met the forces under General\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henry_Clinton_(American_War_of_Independence)" title="Henry Clinton (American War of Independence)">\n        Henry Clinton\n       </a>\n       at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Monmouth" title="Battle of Monmouth">\n        Battle of Monmouth\n       </a>\n       in an indecisive engagement in June 1778. Washington attempted to take the British column by surprise; when the British army attempted to flank the Americans, the Americans retreated in disorder. The ranks were later reorganized and withstood the British charges.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the summer of 1783, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Continental_Congress" title="Continental Congress">\n        Continental Congress\n       </a>\n       met in\n       <a href="/wiki/Nassau_Hall" title="Nassau Hall">\n        Nassau Hall\n       </a>\n       at\n       <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">\n        Princeton University\n       </a>\n       , making Princeton the nation\'s capital for four months. It was there that the Continental Congress learned of the signing of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">\n        Treaty of Paris (1783)\n       </a>\n       , which ended the war.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On December 18, 1787, New Jersey became the third state to ratify the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">\n        United States Constitution\n       </a>\n       , which was overwhelmingly popular in New Jersey, as it prevented New York and Pennsylvania from charging\n       <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">\n        tariffs\n       </a>\n       on goods imported from Europe. On November 20, 1789, the state became the first in the newly formed Union to ratify the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Bill_of_Rights" title="United States Bill of Rights">\n        Bill of Rights\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The 1776\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Jersey_State_Constitution" title="New Jersey State Constitution">\n        New Jersey State Constitution\n       </a>\n       gave the vote to "all inhabitants" who had a certain level of wealth. This included women and blacks, but not married women, because they could not own property separately from their husbands. Both sides, in several elections, claimed that the other side had had unqualified women vote and mocked them for use of "petticoat electors", whether entitled to vote or not; on the other hand, both parties passed Voting Rights Acts. In 1807, the legislature passed a bill interpreting the constitution to mean universal\n       <i>\n        white male\n       </i>\n       <a href="/wiki/Suffrage" title="Suffrage">\n        suffrage\n       </a>\n       , excluding paupers; the constitution was itself an act of the legislature and not enshrined as the modern constitution.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">\n        19th century\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_in_the_19th_century" title="New Jersey in the 19th century">\n        New Jersey in the 19th century\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       On February 15, 1804, New Jersey became the last northern state to\n       <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_States" title="Abolitionism in the United States">\n        abolish\n       </a>\n       new\n       <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">\n        slavery\n       </a>\n       and enacted legislation that slowly phased out existing slavery. This led to a gradual decrease of the slave population. By the close of the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">\n        Civil War\n       </a>\n       , about a dozen African Americans in New Jersey were still held in bondage.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       New Jersey voters initially refused to ratify the constitutional amendments banning slavery and granting rights to the United States\' black population.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1827_Morris_Canal.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1538" data-file-width="3000" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/1827_Morris_Canal.jpg/220px-1827_Morris_Canal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/1827_Morris_Canal.jpg/330px-1827_Morris_Canal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/1827_Morris_Canal.jpg/440px-1827_Morris_Canal.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1827_Morris_Canal.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A map of the 107-mile long\n         <a href="/wiki/Morris_Canal" title="Morris Canal">\n          Morris Canal\n         </a>\n         across northern New Jersey\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrialization" title="Industrialization">\n        Industrialization\n       </a>\n       accelerated in the northern part of the state following completion of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Morris_Canal" title="Morris Canal">\n        Morris Canal\n       </a>\n       in 1831. The canal allowed for coal to be brought from eastern\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">\n        Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Lehigh_Valley" title="Lehigh Valley">\n        Lehigh Valley\n       </a>\n       to northern New Jersey\'s growing industries in\n       <a href="/wiki/Paterson,_New_Jersey" title="Paterson, New Jersey">\n        Paterson\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey" title="Newark, New Jersey">\n        Newark\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jersey_City" title="Jersey City">\n        Jersey City\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1844, the second\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Jersey_State_Constitution" title="New Jersey State Constitution">\n        state constitution\n       </a>\n       was ratified and brought into effect. Counties thereby became districts for the State Senate, and some realignment of boundaries (including the creation of\n       <a href="/wiki/Mercer_County,_New_Jersey" title="Mercer County, New Jersey">\n        Mercer County\n       </a>\n       ) immediately followed. This provision was retained in the 1947 Constitution, but was overturned by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">\n        Supreme Court of the United States\n       </a>\n       in 1962 by the decision\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Baker_v._Carr" title="Baker v. Carr">\n         Baker v. Carr\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       . While the Governorship was stronger than under the 1776 constitution, the constitution of 1844 created many offices that were not responsible to him, or to the people, and it gave him a three-year term, but he could not succeed himself.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey was one of the few Union states (the others being\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">\n        Delaware\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">\n        Kentucky\n       </a>\n       ) to select a candidate other than\n       <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">\n        Abraham Lincoln\n       </a>\n       twice in national elections, and sided with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stephen_Douglas" title="Stephen Douglas">\n        Stephen Douglas\n       </a>\n       (1860) and\n       <a href="/wiki/George_B._McClellan" title="George B. McClellan">\n        George B. McClellan\n       </a>\n       (1864) during their campaigns. McClellan, a native Philadelphian, had New Jersey ties and formally resided in New Jersey at the time; he later became Governor of New Jersey (1878\xe2\x80\x9381). (In New Jersey, the factions of the Democratic party managed an effective coalition in 1860.) During the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">\n        American Civil War\n       </a>\n       , the state was led first by Republican Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Smith_Olden" title="Charles Smith Olden">\n        Charles Smith Olden\n       </a>\n       , then by Democrat\n       <a href="/wiki/Joel_Parker" title="Joel Parker">\n        Joel Parker\n       </a>\n       . During the course of the war, over 80,000 from the state enlisted in the Northern army; unlike many states, including some Northern ones, no battle was fought there.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2014)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Newark_NJ_1874.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1690" data-file-width="2204" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Newark_NJ_1874.jpg/220px-Newark_NJ_1874.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Newark_NJ_1874.jpg/330px-Newark_NJ_1874.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Newark_NJ_1874.jpg/440px-Newark_NJ_1874.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Newark_NJ_1874.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         View of state\'s largest city, Newark, in 1874\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In the\n       <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">\n        Industrial Revolution\n       </a>\n       , cities like\n       <a href="/wiki/Paterson,_New_Jersey" title="Paterson, New Jersey">\n        Paterson\n       </a>\n       grew and prospered. Previously, the economy had been largely agrarian, which was problematically subject to crop failures and poor soil. This caused a shift to a more industrialized economy, one based on manufactured commodities such as textiles and silk.\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_inventors" title="List of inventors">\n        Inventor\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">\n        Thomas Edison\n       </a>\n       also became an important figure of the Industrial Revolution, having been\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Edison_patents" title="List of Edison patents">\n        granted 1,093 patents\n       </a>\n       , many of which for inventions he developed while working in New Jersey. Edison\'s facilities, first at\n       <a href="/wiki/Menlo_Park,_New_Jersey" title="Menlo Park, New Jersey">\n        Menlo Park\n       </a>\n       and then in\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Orange,_New_Jersey" title="West Orange, New Jersey">\n        West Orange\n       </a>\n       , are considered perhaps the first\n       <a href="/wiki/Research_center" title="Research center">\n        research centers\n       </a>\n       in the U.S. Christie Street in Menlo Park was the first thoroughfare in the world to have electric lighting. Transportation was greatly improved as\n       <a href="/wiki/Locomotive" title="Locomotive">\n        locomotion\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Steamboat" title="Steamboat">\n        steamboats\n       </a>\n       were introduced to New Jersey.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Iron_ore" title="Iron ore">\n        Iron\n       </a>\n       mining was also a leading industry during the middle to late 19th century.\n       <a href="/wiki/Bog_iron" title="Bog iron">\n        Bog iron\n       </a>\n       pits in the southern New Jersey Pinelands were among the first sources of iron for the new nation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">\n        Mines\n       </a>\n       such as Mt. Hope, Mine Hill and the Rockaway Valley Mines created a thriving industry. Mining generated the impetus for new towns and was one of the driving forces behind the need for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Morris_Canal" title="Morris Canal">\n        Morris Canal\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">\n        Zinc\n       </a>\n       mines were also a major industry, especially the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sterling_Hill_Mine" title="Sterling Hill Mine">\n        Sterling Hill Mine\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Edison_in_his_NJ_laboratory_1901.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="558" data-file-width="535" height="229" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Edison_in_his_NJ_laboratory_1901.jpg/220px-Edison_in_his_NJ_laboratory_1901.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Edison_in_his_NJ_laboratory_1901.jpg/330px-Edison_in_his_NJ_laboratory_1901.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Edison_in_his_NJ_laboratory_1901.jpg/440px-Edison_in_his_NJ_laboratory_1901.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Edison_in_his_NJ_laboratory_1901.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">\n          Thomas Edison\n         </a>\n         in his laboratory, West Orange, New Jersey, 1901\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">\n        20th century\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_in_the_20th_century" title="New Jersey in the 20th century">\n        New Jersey in the 20th century\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey prospered through the\n       <a href="/wiki/Roaring_Twenties" title="Roaring Twenties">\n        Roaring Twenties\n       </a>\n       . The first\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miss_America_Pageant" title="Miss America Pageant">\n        Miss America Pageant\n       </a>\n       was held in 1921 in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_City" title="Atlantic City">\n        Atlantic City\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Holland_Tunnel" title="Holland Tunnel">\n        Holland Tunnel\n       </a>\n       connecting\n       <a href="/wiki/Jersey_City,_New_Jersey" title="Jersey City, New Jersey">\n        Jersey City\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">\n        Manhattan\n       </a>\n       opened in 1927, and the first\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drive-in_movie" title="Drive-in movie">\n        drive-in movie\n       </a>\n       was shown in 1933 in Camden. During the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">\n        Great Depression\n       </a>\n       of the 1930s, the state offered begging licenses to unemployed residents,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the zeppelin airship\n       <a href="/wiki/Hindenburg_disaster" title="Hindenburg disaster">\n        Hindenburg\n       </a>\n       crashed in flames over\n       <a href="/wiki/Lakehurst,_New_Jersey" title="Lakehurst, New Jersey">\n        Lakehurst\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/SS_Morro_Castle_(1930)" title="SS Morro Castle (1930)">\n        SS\n        <i>\n         Morro Castle\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       beached itself near Asbury Park after going up in flames while at sea.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Through both\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_War" title="World War">\n        World Wars\n       </a>\n       , New Jersey was a center for war production, especially in naval construction, notably at\n       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Shipbuilding_and_Drydock_Company" title="Federal Shipbuilding and Drydock Company">\n        Federal Shipbuilding and Drydock Company\n       </a>\n       . Battleships, cruisers, and destroyers were made in the state. New Jersey manufactured 6.8 percent of total United States military armaments produced during\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">\n        World War II\n       </a>\n       , ranking fifth among the 48 states.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In addition,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Dix,_New_Jersey" title="Fort Dix, New Jersey">\n        Fort Dix\n       </a>\n       (1917) (originally called "Camp Dix"),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dixhist_39-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-dixhist-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Camp_Merritt_(New_Jersey)" title="Camp Merritt (New Jersey)">\n        Camp Merritt\n       </a>\n       (1917)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Camp_Kilmer" title="Camp Kilmer">\n        Camp Kilmer\n       </a>\n       (1941)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       were all constructed to house and train American soldiers through both World Wars. New Jersey also became a principal location for defense in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">\n        Cold War\n       </a>\n       . Fourteen\n       <a href="/wiki/Project_Nike" title="Project Nike">\n        Nike Missile\n       </a>\n       stations were constructed, especially for the defense of New York City and\n       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">\n        Philadelphia\n       </a>\n       , Pennsylvania.\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Motor_Torpedo_Boat_PT-109" title="Motor Torpedo Boat PT-109">\n         PT-109\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , a motor torpedo boat commanded by Lt. (j.g.)\n       <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">\n        John F. Kennedy\n       </a>\n       in World War II, was built at the Elco Boatworks in Bayonne. The aircraft carrier\n       <a href="/wiki/USS_Enterprise_(CV-6)" title="USS Enterprise (CV-6)">\n        USS Enterprise (CV-6)\n       </a>\n       was briefly docked at the Military Ocean Terminal in Bayonne in the 1950s before she was sent to Kearney to be scrapped.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1962, the world\'s first nuclear-powered cargo ship, the\n       <a href="/wiki/NS_Savannah" title="NS Savannah">\n        NS Savannah\n       </a>\n       , was launched at Camden.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Depression-Unemployed-the_Unemployed_Union,_marchers_south_on_Broadway,_Camden_New_Jersey_typical_scene_reflecting..._-_NARA_-_195658.tif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1595" data-file-width="2000" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Depression-Unemployed-the_Unemployed_Union%2C_marchers_south_on_Broadway%2C_Camden_New_Jersey_typical_scene_reflecting..._-_NARA_-_195658.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Depression-Unemployed-the_Unemployed_Union%2C_marchers_south_on_Broadway%2C_Camden_New_Jersey_typical_scene_reflecting..._-_NARA_-_195658.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Depression-Unemployed-the_Unemployed_Union%2C_marchers_south_on_Broadway%2C_Camden_New_Jersey_typical_scene_reflecting..._-_NARA_-_195658.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Depression-Unemployed-the_Unemployed_Union%2C_marchers_south_on_Broadway%2C_Camden_New_Jersey_typical_scene_reflecting..._-_NARA_-_195658.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Depression-Unemployed-the_Unemployed_Union%2C_marchers_south_on_Broadway%2C_Camden_New_Jersey_typical_scene_reflecting..._-_NARA_-_195658.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Depression-Unemployed-the_Unemployed_Union%2C_marchers_south_on_Broadway%2C_Camden_New_Jersey_typical_scene_reflecting..._-_NARA_-_195658.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Depression-Unemployed-the_Unemployed_Union,_marchers_south_on_Broadway,_Camden_New_Jersey_typical_scene_reflecting..._-_NARA_-_195658.tif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Marchers in\n         <a href="/wiki/Camden,_New_Jersey" title="Camden, New Jersey">\n          Camden, New Jersey\n         </a>\n         demanding jobs during the\n         <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression_in_the_United_States" title="Great Depression in the United States">\n          Great Depression\n         </a>\n         , c. 1935\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 1951, the New Jersey Turnpike opened, permitting fast travel by car and truck between North Jersey (and metropolitan New York) and South Jersey (and metropolitan Philadelphia).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the 1960s,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_riot" title="Race riot">\n        race riots\n       </a>\n       erupted in many of the industrial cities of North Jersey. The first race riots in New Jersey occurred in Jersey City on August 2, 1964. Several others ensued in 1967, in\n       <a href="/wiki/1967_Newark_riots" title="1967 Newark riots">\n        Newark\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/1967_Plainfield_riots" title="1967 Plainfield riots">\n        Plainfield\n       </a>\n       . Other riots followed the assassination of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dr._Martin_Luther_King,_Jr." title="Dr. Martin Luther King, Jr.">\n        Dr. Martin Luther King, Jr.\n       </a>\n       in April 1968, just as in the rest of the country. A riot occurred in\n       <a href="/wiki/Camden,_New_Jersey" title="Camden, New Jersey">\n        Camden\n       </a>\n       in 1971.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As a result of an order from the New Jersey Supreme Court to fund schools equitably, the New Jersey legislature passed an income tax bill in 1976. Prior to this bill, the state had no income tax.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tws29decf3354_43-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tws29decf3354-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">\n        21st century\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_in_the_21st_century" title="New Jersey in the 21st century">\n        New Jersey in the 21st century\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In the early part of the 2000s, two\n       <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">\n        light rail\n       </a>\n       systems were opened: the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hudson%E2%80%93Bergen_Light_Rail" title="Hudson\xe2\x80\x93Bergen Light Rail">\n        Hudson\xe2\x80\x93Bergen Light Rail\n       </a>\n       in Hudson County and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/River_Line_(New_Jersey_Transit)" title="River Line (New Jersey Transit)">\n        River Line\n       </a>\n       between Camden and Trenton. The intent of these projects were to encourage\n       <a href="/wiki/Transit-oriented_development" title="Transit-oriented development">\n        transit-oriented development\n       </a>\n       in North Jersey and South Jersey, respectively. The HBLR in particular was credited with a revitalization of Hudson County and\n       <a href="/wiki/Jersey_City,_New_Jersey" title="Jersey City, New Jersey">\n        Jersey City\n       </a>\n       in particular.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Urban revitalization has continued in North Jersey in the 21st century. As of 2014, Jersey City\'s Census-estimated population was 262,146,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEst_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PopEst-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       with the largest population increase of any municipality in New Jersey since 2010,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JC2014Est_49-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-JC2014Est-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       representing an increase of 5.9% from the\n       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">\n        2010 United States Census\n       </a>\n       , when the city\'s population was enumerated at 247,597.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census2010_50-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Census2010-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LWD2010_51-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LWD2010-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In\n       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">\n        2010\n       </a>\n       , Newark experienced its first population increase since the 1950s.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">\n        Geography\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:High_Point_Monument_and_Lake_Marcia_framed.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2119" data-file-width="1626" height="287" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/High_Point_Monument_and_Lake_Marcia_framed.jpg/220px-High_Point_Monument_and_Lake_Marcia_framed.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/High_Point_Monument_and_Lake_Marcia_framed.jpg/330px-High_Point_Monument_and_Lake_Marcia_framed.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/High_Point_Monument_and_Lake_Marcia_framed.jpg/440px-High_Point_Monument_and_Lake_Marcia_framed.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div        <a href="/wiki/Sussex_County,_New_Jersey" title="Sussex County, New Jersey">\n          Sussex County\n         </a>\n         , the\n         <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_elevation"      Hudson River\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" New Jersey">\n          Bergen\n         </a>\n         counties\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:South_Mountain_View.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165"         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Essex_County,_New_Jersey" title="Essex County, New Jersey">\n          Essex County\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bigfalls14w_info.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1420" data-file-width="2286" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Bigfalls14w_info.jpg/220px-Bigfalls14w_info.jpg"
