</ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Wealth">\n        Wealth\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Jersey_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="New Jersey locations by per capita income">\n        New Jersey locations by per capita income\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">\n        Economy\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Jersey_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="New Jersey locations by per capita income">\n        New Jersey locations by per capita income\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1999_NJ_Proof.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="772" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/1999_NJ_Proof.png/220px-1999_NJ_Proof.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/1999_NJ_Proof.png/330px-1999_NJ_Proof.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/1999_NJ_Proof.png/440px-1999_NJ_Proof.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1999_NJ_Proof.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The New Jersey State Quarter, released in 1999, with a depiction of\n         <a href="/wiki/Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware" title="Washington Crossing the Delaware">\n          Washington Crossing the Delaware\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The U.S.\n       <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Economic_Analysis" title="Bureau of Economic Analysis">\n        Bureau of Economic Analysis\n       </a>\n       estimates that New Jersey\'s gross state product in 2010 was $487 billion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">\n        <a href="#cite_note-114">\n         [114]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">\n        <a href="#cite_note-115">\n         [115]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       New Jersey\'s estimated taxpayer burden in 2015 was $59,400 per taxpayer.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Institute_for_Truth_in_Accounting_116-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-The_Institute_for_Truth_in_Accounting-116">\n         [116]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Affluence">\n        Affluence\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_GDP_per_capita_(nominal)" title="List of U.S. states by GDP per capita (nominal)">\n        per capita gross state product\n       </a>\n       in 2008 was $54,699, second in the U.S. and above the national per capita\n       <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">\n        gross domestic product\n       </a>\n       of $46,588.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BEAState_117-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BEAState-117">\n         [117]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Its\n       <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">\n        per capita income\n       </a>\n       was the third highest in the nation with $51,358.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BEAState_117-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BEAState-117">\n         [117]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2013, the state had the second-largest number of millionaires per capita in the United States (ratio of 7.49%), according to a study by Phoenix Marketing International.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">\n        <a href="#cite_note-118">\n         [118]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is ranked 2nd in the nation by the number of places with per capita incomes above national average with 76.4%. Nine of New Jersey\'s counties are in the wealthiest 100 of the country.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Income_by_Location_in_New_Jersey.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="882" data-file-width="750" height="306" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Map_of_Income_by_Location_in_New_Jersey.png/260px-Map_of_Income_by_Location_in_New_Jersey.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Map_of_Income_by_Location_in_New_Jersey.png/390px-Map_of_Income_by_Location_in_New_Jersey.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Map_of_Income_by_Location_in_New_Jersey.png/520px-Map_of_Income_by_Location_in_New_Jersey.png 2x" width="260"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Income_by_Location_in_New_Jersey.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A heat map showing median income distribution by county in New Jersey.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fiscal_policy">\n        Fiscal policy\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey has seven\n       <a href="/wiki/Tax_bracket" title="Tax bracket">\n        tax brackets\n       </a>\n       that determine\n       <a href="/wiki/State_income_tax" title="State income tax">\n        state income tax\n       </a>\n       rates, which range from 1.4% to 8.97%. The standard\n       <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">\n        sales tax\n       </a>\n       rate as of January 1, 2017, is 6.875%, applicable to all retail sales unless specifically exempt by law.\n       <a href="/wiki/Tax_exemption" title="Tax exemption">\n        Tax exemptions\n       </a>\n       include most food items for at-home preparation, medications, most clothing, footwear, and disposable paper products for use in the home. Approximately 30 New Jersey municipalities are designated as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urban_Enterprise_Zone" title="Urban Enterprise Zone">\n        Urban Enterprise Zones\n       </a>\n       , in which shoppers are charged a 3\xc2\xbd%\n       <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">\n        sales tax\n       </a>\n       rate, half of the rate charged outside the UEZs. Sections of\n       <a href="/wiki/Paterson,_New_Jersey" title="Paterson, New Jersey">\n        Paterson\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth,_New_Jersey" title="Elizabeth, New Jersey">\n        Elizabeth\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Jersey_City,_New_Jersey" title="Jersey City, New Jersey">\n        Jersey City\n       </a>\n       are examples of communities that are subject to the lower sales tax rate.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey has the highest cumulative tax rate of all 50 states with residents paying a total of $68 billion in state and local taxes annually with a per capita burden of $7,816 at a rate of 12.9% of income.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">\n        <a href="#cite_note-119">\n         [119]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       All\n       <a href="/wiki/Real_property" title="Real property">\n        real property\n       </a>\n       located in the state is subject to\n       <a href="/wiki/Property_tax" title="Property tax">\n        property tax\n       </a>\n       unless specifically exempted by statute. New Jersey does not assess an intangible personal property tax, but it does impose an\n       <a href="/wiki/Inheritance_tax" title="Inheritance tax">\n        inheritance tax\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_taxation_disparity">\n        Federal taxation disparity\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey consistently ranks as having one of the highest proportional levels of disparity of any state in the United States based upon what it receives from the federal government relative to what it gives. In 2015, WalletHub ranked New Jersey the state least dependent upon federal government aid overall and having the fourth lowest return on taxpayer investment from the federal government, at 48 cents per dollar.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">\n        <a href="#cite_note-120">\n         [120]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey has one of the highest tax burdens in the nation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taxfoundation_121-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-taxfoundation-121">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Factors for this include the large federal tax liability which is not adjusted for New Jersey\'s higher cost of living and Medicaid funding formulas. As shown by the study, incomes tend to be higher in New Jersey, which puts those in higher tax brackets especially vulnerable to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Alternative_minimum_tax" title="Alternative minimum tax">\n        alternative minimum tax\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Industries">\n        Industries\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cranberrys_beim_Ernten.jpeg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2125" data-file-width="3157" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Cranberrys_beim_Ernten.jpeg/220px-Cranberrys_beim_Ernten.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Cranberrys_beim_Ernten.jpeg/330px-Cranberrys_beim_Ernten.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Cranberrys_beim_Ernten.jpeg/440px-Cranberrys_beim_Ernten.jpeg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cranberrys_beim_Ernten.jpeg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Cranberry" title="Cranberry">\n          Cranberry\n         </a>\n         harvest\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biotech_and_pharmaceutical_companies_in_New_Jersey" title="Biotech and pharmaceutical companies in New Jersey">\n        Biotech and pharmaceutical companies in New Jersey\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey\'s economy is multifaceted but is nevertheless centered upon the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_industry" title="Pharmaceutical industry">\n        pharmaceutical industry\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Financial_industry" title="Financial industry">\n        financial industry\n       </a>\n       , chemical development,\n       <a href="/wiki/Telecommunication" title="Telecommunication">\n        telecommunications\n       </a>\n       , food processing, electric equipment, printing, publishing, and tourism. New Jersey\'s agricultural outputs are nursery stock, horses, vegetables, fruits and nuts, seafood, and dairy products.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">\n        <a href="#cite_note-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       New Jersey ranks second among states in\n       <a href="/wiki/Blueberry" title="Blueberry">\n        blueberry\n       </a>\n       production, third in\n       <a href="/wiki/Cranberry" title="Cranberry">\n        cranberries\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Spinach" title="Spinach">\n        spinach\n       </a>\n       , and fourth in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bell_peppers" title="Bell peppers">\n        bell peppers\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Peach" title="Peach">\n        peaches\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Lettuce" title="Lettuce">\n        head lettuce\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">\n        <a href="#cite_note-123">\n         [123]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       New Jersey harvests the fourth-largest number of acres planted with asparagus.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">\n        <a href="#cite_note-124">\n         [124]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Although New Jersey is home to many energy-intensive industries, its energy consumption is only 2.7% of the U.S. total, and its\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_emissions" title="Carbon dioxide emissions">\n        carbon dioxide emissions\n       </a>\n       are 0.8% of the U.S. total. Its comparatively low\n       <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">\n        greenhouse gas\n       </a>\n       emissions can be attributed to nuclear power. According to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Energy_Information_Administration" title="Energy Information Administration">\n        Energy Information Administration\n       </a>\n       , nuclear power dominates New Jersey\'s electricity market, typically supplying more than one-half of State generation. New Jersey has three nuclear power plants, including the\n       <a href="/wiki/Oyster_Creek_Nuclear_Generating_Station" title="Oyster Creek Nuclear Generating Station">\n        Oyster Creek Nuclear Generating Station\n       </a>\n       , which came online in 1969 and is the oldest operating nuclear plant in the country.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">\n        <a href="#cite_note-125">\n         [125]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey has a strong scientific economy and is home to major pharmaceutical and telecommunications firms. There is also a strong service economy in New Jersey serving residents who work in New York City or Philadelphia in retail sales, education, and real estate. Furthermore, New Jersey draws upon its large and well-educated labor pool, which also supports the myriad of industries that exists today.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Shipping is a strong industry in New Jersey because of the state\'s strategic geographic location, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_New_York_and_New_Jersey" title="Port of New York and New Jersey">\n        Port of New York and New Jersey\n       </a>\n       being the busiest\n       <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">\n        port\n       </a>\n       on the\n       <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">\n        East Coast\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port_Newark-Elizabeth_Marine_Terminal" title="Port Newark-Elizabeth Marine Terminal">\n        Port Newark-Elizabeth Marine Terminal\n       </a>\n       was the world\'s first\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Container_port" title="Container port">\n        container port\n       </a>\n       and is one of the world\'s largest container ports. New Jersey also has a strong presence in chemical development, refining, and food processing operations.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey hosts several business headquarters, including twenty-four\n       <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">\n        Fortune 500\n       </a>\n       companies.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">\n        <a href="#cite_note-126">\n         [126]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Paramus,_New_Jersey" title="Paramus, New Jersey">\n        Paramus\n       </a>\n       in Bergen County has become the top retail\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zip_code" title="Zip code">\n        zip code\n       </a>\n       (07652) in the United States, with the municipality generating over $5 billion in annual retail sales.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">\n        <a href="#cite_note-127">\n         [127]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">\n        <a href="#cite_note-128">\n         [128]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Several New Jersey counties such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Somerset_County,_New_Jersey" title="Somerset County, New Jersey">\n        Somerset\n       </a>\n       (7),\n       <a href="/wiki/Morris_County,_New_Jersey" title="Morris County, New Jersey">\n        Morris\n       </a>\n       (10),\n       <a href="/wiki/Hunterdon_County,_New_Jersey" title="Hunterdon County, New Jersey">\n        Hunterdon\n       </a>\n       (13),\n       <a href="/wiki/Bergen_County,_New_Jersey" title="Bergen County, New Jersey">\n        Bergen\n       </a>\n       (21),\n       <a href="/wiki/Monmouth_County,_New_Jersey" title="Monmouth County, New Jersey">\n        Monmouth\n       </a>\n       (42) counties are ranked among the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Highest-income_counties_in_the_United_States" title="Highest-income counties in the United States">\n        highest-income counties in the United States\n       </a>\n       . Four others are also in the top 100.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">\n        Tourism\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Atlantic_City_skyline_from_47th_floor_of_Revel.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Atlantic_City_skyline_from_47th_floor_of_Revel.jpg/220px-Atlantic_City_skyline_from_47th_floor_of_Revel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Atlantic_City_skyline_from_47th_floor_of_Revel.jpg/330px-Atlantic_City_skyline_from_47th_floor_of_Revel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Atlantic_City_skyline_from_47th_floor_of_Revel.jpg/440px-Atlantic_City_skyline_from_47th_floor_of_Revel.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Atlantic_City_skyline_from_47th_floor_of_Revel.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_City" title="Atlantic City">\n          Atlantic City\n         </a>\n         , looking southward, is an\n         <a href="/wiki/Seaside_resort" title="Seaside resort">\n          oceanfront resort\n         </a>\n         and the nexus of New Jersey\'s\n         <a href="/wiki/Casino" title="Casino">\n          gaming industry\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey\'s location as a crossroads of commerce and its extensive transportation system have put over one third of all United States residents and many\n       <a href="/wiki/Canadians" title="Canadians">\n        Canadian\n       </a>\n       residents within overnight distance by land. This accessibility to consumer revenue has enabled\n       <a href="/wiki/Seaside_resort" title="Seaside resort">\n        seaside resorts\n       </a>\n       such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_City,_New_Jersey" title="Atlantic City, New Jersey">\n        Atlantic City\n       </a>\n       and the remainder of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Jersey_Shore" title="Jersey Shore">\n        Jersey Shore\n       </a>\n       , as well as the state\'s other natural and cultural attractions, to contribute significantly to New Jersey\'s record tourism revenue of $43.4 billion and 95 million tourist visitations in 2015, directly supporting 318,330 jobs and sustaining more than 512,000 jobs including peripheral impacts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">\n        <a href="#cite_note-129">\n         [129]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Gambling">\n        Gambling\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Gambling_in_New_Jersey" title="Gambling in New Jersey">\n        Gambling in New Jersey\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 1976, a referendum of New Jersey voters approved\n       <a href="/wiki/Casino" title="Casino">\n        casino\n       </a>\n       gambling in Atlantic City, where the first legalized casino opened in 1978.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">\n        <a href="#cite_note-130">\n         [130]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       At that time,\n       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">\n        Las Vegas\n       </a>\n       was the only mega-casino resort in the country.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">\n        <a href="#cite_note-131">\n         [131]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Several casinos lie along the Atlantic City\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_City#Boardwalk" title="Atlantic City">\n        Boardwalk\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-acbrdwlk_132-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-acbrdwlk-132">\n         [132]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the first and longest boardwalk in the world.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-visitnj_133-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-visitnj-133">\n         [133]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On February 26, 2013, Governor Chris Christie signed\n       <a href="/wiki/Online_gambling" title="Online gambling">\n        online gambling\n       </a>\n       into law.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">\n        <a href="#cite_note-134">\n         [134]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Atlantic City experienced a dramatic contraction in its stature as a gambling destination after 2010, including the closure of multiple casinos since 2014, spurred by competition from the advent of legalized gambling in other northeastern U.S. states.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">\n        <a href="#cite_note-135">\n         [135]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">\n        <a href="#cite_note-136">\n         [136]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_resources">\n        Natural resources\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Forest" title="Forest">\n        Forests\n       </a>\n       cover 45%, or approximately 2.1 million acres, of New Jersey\'s land area.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">\n        <a href="#cite_note-137">\n         [137]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The chief tree of the northern forests is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">\n        oak\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/Pine_Barrens_(New_Jersey)" title="Pine Barrens (New Jersey)">\n        Pine Barrens\n       </a>\n       , consisting of\n       <a href="/wiki/Pine" title="Pine">\n        pine\n       </a>\n       forests, is in the southern part of the state.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Some mining activity of\n       <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">\n        zinc\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Iron" title="Iron">\n        iron\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">\n        manganese\n       </a>\n       still takes place in the area in and around the\n       <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Furnace" title="Franklin Furnace">\n        Franklin Furnace\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey is second in the nation in\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_New_Jersey" title="Solar power in New Jersey">\n        solar power\n       </a>\n       installations,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">\n        <a href="#cite_note-138">\n         [138]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       enabled by one of the country\'s most favorable\n       <a href="/wiki/Net_metering" title="Net metering">\n        net metering\n       </a>\n       policies, and the renewable energy certificates program. The state has more than 10,000 solar installations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">\n        <a href="#cite_note-139">\n         [139]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">\n        Education\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post-secondary_education_in_New_Jersey" title="Post-secondary education in New Jersey">\n        Post-secondary education in New Jersey\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Primary_education_in_the_United_States" title="Primary education in the United States">\n        Primary education in the United States\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education_in_the_United_States" title="Secondary education in the United States">\n        Secondary education in the United States\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Higher_education_in_the_United_States" title="Higher education in the United States">\n        Higher education in the United States\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_United_States" title="Education in the United States">\n        Education in the United States\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bishop_House-Rutgers_University.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Bishop_House-Rutgers_University.jpg/440px-Bishop_House-Rutgers_University.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bishop_House-Rutgers_University.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Bishop House at\n         <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_University" title="Rutgers University">\n          Rutgers University\n         </a>\n         , which in 2013 gained\n         <a href="/wiki/Medical_school" title="Medical school">\n          medical\n         </a>\n         and\n         <a href="/wiki/Dental_school" title="Dental school">\n          dental schools\n         </a>\n         intended to augment its profile as a national\n         <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university">\n          research university\n         </a>\n         .\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RutgersRef_140-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-RutgersRef-140">\n           [140]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Princeton_(6035183309).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Princeton_%286035183309%29.jpg/220px-Princeton_%286035183309%29.jpg" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Princeton_%286035183309%29.jpg/440px-Princeton_%286035183309%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Princeton_(6035183309).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Cleveland Tower dominates the skyline of\n         <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University_Graduate_College" title="Princeton University Graduate College">\n          Princeton University Graduate College\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 2010, there were 605\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_school_districts_in_New_Jersey" title="List of school districts in New Jersey">\n        school districts in the state\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wp100422_141-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wp100422-141">\n         [141]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Secretary of Education Rick Rosenberg, appointed by Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Jon_Corzine" title="Jon Corzine">\n        Jon Corzine\n       </a>\n       , created the Education Advancement Initiative (EAI) to increase college admission rates by 10% for New Jersey\'s high school students, decrease dropout rates by 15%, and increase the amount of money devoted to schools by 10%. Rosenberg retracted this plan when criticized for taking the money out of healthcare to fund this initiative.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2010 the state government paid all of the teachers\' premiums for health insurance,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wp100422_141-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wp100422-141">\n         [141]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but currently all NJ public teachers pay a portion of their own health insurance premiums.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Census data reveal that New Jersey spent more per each public school student than any other state except New York in 2009, amounting to $16,271 spent per pupil, with 41% of the revenue derived from state sources.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">\n        <a href="#cite_note-142">\n         [142]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       According to 2011\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">\n         Newsweek\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       statistics, students of\n       <a href="/wiki/High_Technology_High_School" title="High Technology High School">\n        High Technology High School\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Lincroft,_New_Jersey" title="Lincroft, New Jersey">\n        Lincroft\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Monmouth_County,_New_Jersey" title="Monmouth County, New Jersey">\n        Monmouth County\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Bergen_County_Academies" title="Bergen County Academies">\n        Bergen County Academies\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Hackensack,_New_Jersey" title="Hackensack, New Jersey">\n        Hackensack\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bergen_County,_New_Jersey" title="Bergen County, New Jersey">\n        Bergen County\n       </a>\n       registered average\n       <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">\n        SAT\n       </a>\n       scores of 2145 and 2100, respectively,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsweekHS2011_143-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-newsweekHS2011-143">\n         [143]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       representing the second- and third-highest scores, respectively, of all listed U.S. high schools.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsweekHS2011_143-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-newsweekHS2011-143">\n         [143]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">\n        Princeton University\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Princeton,_New_Jersey" title="Princeton, New Jersey">\n        Princeton\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mercer_County,_New_Jersey" title="Mercer County, New Jersey">\n        Mercer County\n       </a>\n       , was ranked the top U.S. national university per the 2018 list of\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">\n         U.S. News &amp; World Report\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">\n        <a href="#cite_note-144">\n         [144]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2013,\n       <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_University" title="Rutgers University">\n        Rutgers University\n       </a>\n       gained\n       <a href="/wiki/Medical_school" title="Medical school">\n        medical\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Dental_school" title="Dental school">\n        dental schools\n       </a>\n       intended to augment its profile as a national\n       <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university">\n        research university\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RutgersRef_140-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-RutgersRef-140">\n         [140]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2014, New Jersey\'s school systems were ranked at the top of all fifty U.S. states by financial\n       <a href="/wiki/Website" title="Website">\n        website\n       </a>\n       Wallethub.com.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">\n        <a href="#cite_note-145">\n         [145]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Nine New Jersey high schools were ranked among the top 25 in the U.S. on the\n       <i>\n        Newsweek\n       </i>\n       "America\'s Top High Schools 2016" list, more than from any other state.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">\n        <a href="#cite_note-146">\n         [146]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_communication">\n        Media and communication\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image"        New Jersey\'s area codes\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Newspapers">\n        Newspapers\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Major New Jersey newspapers including the following:\n      </p>\n      <div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 20em; -webkit-column-width: 20em; column-width: 20em;">\n       <ul>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Asbury_Park_Press" title="Asbury Park Press">\n           Asbury Park Press\n          </a>\n         </i>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Burlington_County_Times" title="Burlington County Times">\n           Burlington County Times\n          </a>\n         </i>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Courier_News_(New_Jersey)" title="Courier News (New Jersey)">\n           Courier News\n          </a>\n         </i>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Courier-Post" title="Courier-Post">\n           Courier-Post\n          </a>\n         </i>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          Cranford Chronicle\n         </i>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Daily_Record_(Morristown)" title="Daily Record (Morristown)">\n           Daily Record\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         (Morristown)\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">\n          <a href="#cite_note-147">\n           [147]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/The_Express-Times" title="The Express-Times">\n           The Express-Times\n          </a>\n         </i>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Gloucester_County_Times" title="Gloucester County Times">\n           Gloucester County Times\n          </a>\n         </i>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Herald_News" title="Herald News">\n           Herald News\n          </a>\n         </i>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Home_News_Tribune" Independent Press\n         </i>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jersey_Journal" title="Jersey Journal">\n           Jersey Journal\n          </a>\n         </i>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_New_Jersey_Herald" title="The New Jersey Herald">\n           The New Jersey Herald\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">\n          <a href="#cite_note-148">\n           [148]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/The_News_of_Cumberland_County" title="The News of Cumberland County">\n           The News of Cumberland County\n          </a>\n         </i>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/The_Press_of_Atlantic_City" title="The Press of Atlantic City">\n           The Press of Atlantic City\n          </a>\n         </i>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/The_Record_(Bergen_County)" title="The Record (Bergen County)">\n           The Record\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">\n          <a href="#cite_note-149">\n           [149]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          The Record-Press and Suburban News\n         </i>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          The Reporter\n         </i>\n         (Somerset)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/The_Star-Ledger" title="The Star-Ledger">\n           The Star-Ledger\n          </a>\n         </i>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/The_Times_(Trenton)" title="The Times (Trenton)">\n          <i>\n           The Times\n          </i>\n          (Trenton)\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Today%27s_Sunbeam" title="Today\'s Sunbeam">\n           Today\'s Sunbeam\n          </a>\n         </i>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trentonian" title="Trentonian">\n           Trentonian\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         (Mercer)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <i>\n          The Warren Reporter\n         </i>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Online_news">\n        Online news\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Since 2006 there have been a growing number of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyperlocal_news" title="Hyperlocal news">\n        hyperlocal news\n       </a>\n       sites, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Patch_Media" title="Patch Media">\n        Patch\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">\n        <a href="#cite_note-150">\n         [150]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jersey_Hyperlocals_151-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Jersey_Hyperlocals-151">\n         [151]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These sites provide relevant news for their respective communities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NJMonthly_152-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NJMonthly-152">\n         [152]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_stations">\n        Radio stations\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_radio_stations_in_New_Jersey" title="List of radio stations in New Jersey">\n        List of radio stations in New Jersey\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Television_and_film">\n        Television and film\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Television_and_film_of_New_Jersey" title="Television and film of New Jersey">\n        Television and film of New Jersey\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Motion picture technology was developed by\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">\n        Thomas Edison\n       </a>\n       , with much of his early work done at his\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Orange,_New_Jersey" title="West Orange, New Jersey">\n        West Orange\n       </a>\n       laboratory.\n       <a href="/wiki/Edison%27s_Black_Maria" title="Edison\'s Black Maria">\n        Edison\'s Black Maria\n       </a>\n       was the first motion picture studio.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/America%27s_first_motion_picture_industry" title="America\'s first motion picture industry">\n        America\'s first motion picture industry\n       </a>\n       started in 1907 in\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lee,_New_Jersey" title="Fort Lee, New Jersey">\n        Fort Lee\n       </a>\n       and the first studio was constructed there in 1909.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">\n        <a href="#cite_note-153">\n         [153]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/DuMont_Laboratories" title="DuMont Laboratories">\n        DuMont Laboratories\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Passaic,_New_Jersey" title="Passaic, New Jersey">\n        Passaic\n       </a>\n       developed early sets and made the first broadcast to the private home.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A number of television shows and films have been filmed in New Jersey. Since 1978, the state has maintained a Motion Picture and Television Commission to encourage filming in-state.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">\n        <a href="#cite_note-154">\n         [154]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       New Jersey has long offered tax credits to television producers. Governor Chris Christie suspended the credits in 2010, but the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Jersey_State_Legislature" title="New Jersey State Legislature">\n        New Jersey State Legislature\n       </a>\n       in 2011 approved the restoration and expansion of the tax credit program. Under bills passed by both the state Senate and Assembly, the program offers 20 percent tax credits (22% in\n       <a href="/wiki/Urban_enterprise_zone" title="Urban enterprise zone">\n        urban enterprise zones\n       </a>\n       ) to television and film productions that shoot in the state and meet set standards for hiring and local spending.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crewsback_155-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-crewsback-155">\n         [155]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">\n        Transportation\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_New_Jersey" title="Transportation in New Jersey">\n        Transportation in New Jersey\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Roadways">\n        Roadways\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_New_Jersey_NA.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1640" data-file-width="2122" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Map_of_New_Jersey_NA.png/220px-Map_of_New_Jersey_NA.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Map_of_New_Jersey_NA.png/330px-Map_of_New_Jersey_NA.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Map_of_New_Jersey_NA.png/440px-Map_of_New_Jersey_NA.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_New_Jersey_NA.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Map of New Jersey showing major transportation networks and cities\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:George_Washington_Bridge_from_New_Jersey-edit.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="727" data-file-width="738" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/George_Washington_Bridge_from_New_Jersey-edit.jpg/220px-George_Washington_Bridge_from_New_Jersey-edit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/George_Washington_Bridge_from_New_Jersey-edit.jpg/330px-George_Washington_Bridge_from_New_Jersey-edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/George_Washington_Bridge_from_New_Jersey-edit.jpg/440px-George_Washington_Bridge_from_New_Jersey-edit.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:George_Washington_Bridge_from_New_Jersey-edit.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_Bridge" title="George Washington Bridge">\n          George Washington Bridge\n         </a>\n         , connecting\n         <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lee,_New_Jersey" title="Fort Lee, New Jersey">\n          Fort Lee\n         </a>\n         (foreground) in\n         <a href="/wiki/Bergen_County,_New_Jersey" title="Bergen County, New Jersey">\n          Bergen County\n         </a>\n         across the\n         <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">\n          Hudson River\n         </a>\n         to\n         <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">\n          New York City\n         </a>\n         , is the world\'s busiest motor vehicle bridge.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-panynj.gov_156-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-panynj.gov-156">\n           [156]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abcgwb_157-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-abcgwb-157">\n           [157]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_New_Jersey_State_Highways" title="List of New Jersey State Highways">\n        List of New Jersey State Highways\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Turnpike" title="New Jersey Turnpike">\n        New Jersey Turnpike\n       </a>\n       is one of the most prominent and heavily trafficked roadways in the United States. This\n       <a href="/wiki/Toll_road" title="Toll road">\n        toll road\n       </a>\n       carries\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_New_Jersey" title="Interstate 95 in New Jersey">\n        Interstate 95\n       </a>\n       traffic between\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">\n        Delaware\n       </a>\n       and New York, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">\n        East Coast\n       </a>\n       in general. Commonly referred to as simply "the Turnpike," it is known for its numerous\n       <a href="/wiki/Rest_area" title="Rest area">\n        rest areas\n       </a>\n       named after prominent New Jerseyans as diverse as inventor\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">\n        Thomas Edison\n       </a>\n       ; United States Secretary of the Treasury\n       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton" title="Alexander Hamilton">\n        Alexander Hamilton\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidents_of_the_United_States" title="Presidents of the United States">\n        United States Presidents\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Grover_Cleveland" title="Grover Cleveland">\n        Grover Cleveland\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">\n        Woodrow Wilson\n       </a>\n       ; writers\n       <a href="/wiki/James_Fenimore_Cooper" title="James Fenimore Cooper">\n        James Fenimore Cooper\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Joyce_Kilmer" title="Joyce Kilmer">\n        Joyce Kilmer\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Walt_Whitman" title="Walt Whitman">\n        Walt Whitman\n       </a>\n       ; patriot\n       <a href="/wiki/Molly_Pitcher" title="Molly Pitcher">\n        Molly Pitcher\n       </a>\n       ; Red Cross founder\n       <a href="/wiki/Clara_Barton" title="Clara Barton">\n        Clara Barton\n       </a>\n       ; and football coach\n       <a href="/wiki/Vince_Lombardi" title="Vince Lombardi">\n        Vince Lombardi\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Garden_State_Parkway" title="Garden State Parkway">\n        Garden State Parkway\n       </a>\n       , or simply "the Parkway," carries relatively more in-state traffic than interstate traffic and runs from the town of\n       <a href="/wiki/Montvale,_New_Jersey" title="Montvale, New Jersey">\n        Montvale\n       </a>\n       along New Jersey\'s northern border to its southernmost tip at\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_May,_New_Jersey" title="Cape May, New Jersey">\n        Cape May\n       </a>\n       for 172.4 miles (277.5\xc2\xa0km). It is the trunk that connects the New York metropolitan area to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Jersey_Shore" title="Jersey Shore">\n        Jersey Shore\n       </a>\n       and is consistently one of the safest roads in the nation. With a total of 15 travel and 6 shoulder lanes, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Driscoll_Bridge" title="Driscoll Bridge">\n        Driscoll Bridge\n       </a>\n       on the Parkway, spanning the\n       <a href="/wiki/Raritan_River" title="Raritan River">\n        Raritan River\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Middlesex_County,_New_Jersey" title="Middlesex County, New Jersey">\n        Middlesex County\n       </a>\n       , is the widest motor vehicle bridge in the world by number of lanes\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">\n        <a href="#cite_note-158">\n         [158]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       as well as one of the busiest.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey is connected to New York City via various\n       <a href="/wiki/Bridge" title="Bridge">\n        bridges\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tunnel" title="Tunnel">\n        tunnels\n       </a>\n       . The double-decked\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_Bridge" title="George Washington Bridge">\n        George Washington Bridge\n       </a>\n       carries the heaviest load of motor vehicle traffic of any bridge in the world,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-panynj.gov_156-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-panynj.gov-156">\n         [156]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abcgwb_157-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-abcgwb-157">\n         [157]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       at 102 million vehicles per year, over fourteen lanes, from\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lee,_New_Jersey" title="Fort Lee, New Jersey">\n        Fort Lee, New Jersey\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bergen_County" title="Bergen County">\n        Bergen County\n       </a>\n       across the Hudson River to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Trans-Manhattan_Expressway" title="Trans-Manhattan Expressway">\n        Trans-Manhattan Expressway\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington_Heights,_Manhattan" title="Washington Heights, Manhattan">\n        Washington Heights\n       </a>\n       neighborhood of\n       <a href="/wiki/Upper_Manhattan" title="Upper Manhattan">\n        Upper Manhattan\n       </a>\n       in New York City;\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95" title="Interstate 95">\n        Interstate 95\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1/9" title="U.S. Route 1/9">\n        U.S. Route 1/9\n       </a>\n       cross the Hudson River via the "GWB", while\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_46" title="U.S. Route 46">\n        U.S. Route 46\n       </a>\n       , which lies entirely within New Jersey, ends halfway across the bridge at the state border with New York. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Tunnel" title="Lincoln Tunnel">\n        Lincoln Tunnel\n       </a>\n       connects to\n       <a href="/wiki/Midtown_Manhattan" title="Midtown Manhattan">\n        Midtown Manhattan\n       </a>\n       carrying New Jersey State Route 495 and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Holland_Tunnel" title="Holland Tunnel">\n        Holland Tunnel\n       </a>\n       connects to\n       <a href="/wiki/Lower_Manhattan" title="Lower Manhattan">\n        Lower Manhattan\n       </a>\n       carrying\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_78_in_New_Jersey" title="Interstate 78 in New Jersey">\n        Interstate 78\n       </a>\n       . New Jersey is also connected to\n       <a href="/wiki/Staten_Island" title="Staten Island">\n        Staten Island\n       </a>\n       by three bridges\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 from south to north: the\n       <a href="/wiki/Outerbridge_Crossing" title="Outerbridge Crossing">\n        Outerbridge Crossing\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Goethals_Bridge" title="Goethals Bridge">\n        Goethals Bridge\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Bayonne_Bridge" title="Bayonne Bridge">\n        Bayonne Bridge\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Other expressways in New Jersey include the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_City_Expressway" title="Atlantic City Expressway">\n        Atlantic City Expressway\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Palisades_Interstate_Parkway" title="Palisades Interstate Parkway">\n        Palisades Interstate Parkway\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_76_(east)" title="Interstate 76 (east)">\n        Interstate 76\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_78_in_New_Jersey" title="Interstate 78 in New Jersey">\n        Interstate 78\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_80_in_New_Jersey" title="Interstate 80 in New Jersey">\n        Interstate 80\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_95_(New_Jersey)" title="Interstate 95 (New Jersey)">\n        Interstate 95\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_195_(New_Jersey)" title="Interstate 195 (New Jersey)">\n        Interstate 195\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_278" title="Interstate 278">\n        Interstate 278\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_280_(New_Jersey)" title="Interstate 280 (New Jersey)">\n        Interstate 280\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_287" title="Interstate 287">\n        Interstate 287\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_295_(Delaware-New_Jersey-Pennsylvania)" title="Interstate 295 (Delaware-New Jersey-Pennsylvania)">\n        Interstate 295\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_676" title="Interstate 676">\n        Interstate 676\n       </a>\n       . Other major roadways include\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1_in_New_Jersey" title="U.S. Route 1 in New Jersey">\n        U.S. 1\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Route_4" title="New Jersey Route 4">\n        New Jersey Route 4\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_9_in_New_Jersey" title="U.S. Route 9 in New Jersey">\n        U.S. 9\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Route_10" title="New Jersey Route 10">\n        New Jersey Route 10\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Route_17" title="New Jersey Route 17">\n        New Jersey Route 17\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey has\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_compact" title="Interstate compact">\n        interstate compacts\n       </a>\n       with all three of its neighboring states. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_Authority_of_New_York_and_New_Jersey" title="Port Authority of New York and New Jersey">\n        Port Authority of New York and New Jersey\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River_Port_Authority" title="Delaware River Port Authority">\n        Delaware River Port Authority\n       </a>\n       (with Pennsylvania), and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River_and_Bay_Authority" title="Delaware River and Bay Authority">\n        Delaware River and Bay Authority\n       </a>\n       (with Delaware) operate most of the major transportation routes into and out of New Jersey. Bridge tolls are collected in one direction only \xe2\x80\x93 it is free to cross into New Jersey, but motorists must pay when exiting the state. Exceptions to this are the\n       <a href="/wiki/Dingman%27s_Ferry_Bridge" title="Dingman\'s Ferry Bridge">\n        Dingman\'s Ferry Bridge\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delaware_River_%E2%80%93_Turnpike_Toll_Bridge" title="Delaware River \xe2\x80\x93 Turnpike Toll Bridge">\n        Delaware River \xe2\x80\x93 Turnpike Toll Bridge\n       </a>\n       where tolls are charged both ways. The Washington Crossing and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scudders_Falls_Bridge" title="Scudders Falls Bridge">\n        Scudders Falls (on I-95)\n       </a>\n       bridges near Trenton, as well as Trenton\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Calhoun_Street_Bridge" title="Calhoun Street Bridge">\n        Calhoun Street\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Lower_Trenton_Bridge" title="Lower Trenton Bridge">\n        Bridge Street ("Trenton Makes")\n       </a>\n       bridges, are toll-free. In addition,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riverton-Belvidere_Bridge" title="Riverton-Belvidere Bridge">\n        Riverton-Belvidere Bridge\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Northampton_Street_Bridge" title="Northampton Street Bridge">\n        Northampton Street Bridge\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Riegelsville_Bridge" title="Riegelsville Bridge">\n        Riegelsville Bridge\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper_Black_Eddy-Milford_Bridge" title="Upper Black Eddy-Milford Bridge">\n        Upper Black Eddy-Milford Bridge\n       </a>\n       are free Delaware River bridges into and out of NJ.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey became the only U.S. state where all fuel dispensing stations are required to sell\n       <a href="/wiki/Filling_station" title="Filling station">\n        full-service gasoline\n       </a>\n       to customers at all times, after\n       <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">\n        Oregon\n       </a>\n       \'s introduction of restricted self-service gasoline availability took effect in 2016.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">\n        <a href="#cite_note-159">\n         [159]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is unlawful for a customer to serve oneself gasoline in New Jersey.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">\n        Airports\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NewarkIntAirport.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/NewarkIntAirport.jpg/220px-NewarkIntAirport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/NewarkIntAirport.jpg/330px-NewarkIntAirport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/NewarkIntAirport.jpg/440px-NewarkIntAirport.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NewarkIntAirport.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         New York City skyline from Continental (now United) Terminal C in\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_Airport" title="Newark Liberty Airport">\n          Newark Liberty Airport\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">\n        Newark Liberty International Airport\n       </a>\n       is one of the busiest airports in the United States. Operated by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_Authority_of_New_York_and_New_Jersey" title="Port Authority of New York and New Jersey">\n        Port Authority of New York and New Jersey\n       </a>\n       , which runs the other two major airports in the\n       <a href="/wiki/New_York_metropolitan_area" title="New York metropolitan area">\n        New York metropolitan area\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">\n        John F. Kennedy International Airport\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/LaGuardia_Airport" title="LaGuardia Airport">\n        LaGuardia Airport\n       </a>\n       ), it is one of the three main airports serving the New York City area.\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">\n        United Airlines\n       </a>\n       is the facility\'s largest tenant, operating an entire terminal at Newark, which it uses as one of its primary\n       <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">\n        hubs\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/FedEx_Express" title="FedEx Express">\n        FedEx Express\n       </a>\n       operates a large cargo hub there as well. The adjacent\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport_(NJT_station)" title="Newark Liberty International Airport (NJT station)">\n        Newark Airport railroad station\n       </a>\n       provides access to the trains of\n       <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">\n        Amtrak\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/NJ_Transit" title="NJ Transit">\n        NJ Transit\n       </a>\n       along the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Corridor_Line" title="Northeast Corridor Line">\n        Northeast Corridor Line\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Two smaller commercial airports,\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_City_International_Airport" title="Atlantic City International Airport">\n        Atlantic City International Airport\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trenton-Mercer_Airport" title="Trenton-Mercer Airport">\n        Trenton-Mercer Airport\n       </a>\n       , also operate in other parts of New Jersey.\n       <a href="/wiki/Teterboro_Airport" title="Teterboro Airport">\n        Teterboro Airport\n       </a>\n       , in\n       <a href="/wiki/Bergen_County,_New_Jersey" title="Bergen County, New Jersey">\n        Bergen County\n       </a>\n       , is a\n       <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">\n        general aviation\n       </a>\n       airport popular with private and corporate aircraft, due to its proximity to New York City.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Millville_Municipal_Airport" title="Millville Municipal Airport">\n        Millville Municipal Airport\n       </a>\n       , in\n       <a href="/wiki/Cumberland_County,_New_Jersey" title="Cumberland County, New Jersey">\n        Cumberland County\n       </a>\n       , is a\n       <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">\n        general aviation\n       </a>\n       airport popular with private and corporate aircraft, due to its proximity to the shore.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_and_bus">\n        Rail and bus\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Transit" title="New Jersey Transit">\n        New Jersey Transit\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Transit_Bus_Operations" title="New Jersey Transit Bus Operations">\n        New Jersey Transit Bus Operations\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Transit_Rail_Operations" title="New Jersey Transit Rail Operations">\n        New Jersey Transit Rail Operations\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port_Authority_Trans-Hudson" title="Port Authority Trans-Hudson">\n        Port Authority Trans-Hudson\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/PATCO_Speedline" title="PATCO Speedline">\n        PATCO Speedline\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NECtrain3967.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/NECtrain3967.jpg/220px-NECtrain3967.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/NECtrain3967.jpg/330px-NECtrain3967.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/NECtrain3967.jpg/440px-NECtrain3967.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NECtrain3967.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A\n         <a href="/wiki/NJ_Transit" title="NJ Transit">\n          NJ Transit\n         </a>\n         train heads down the\n         <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Corridor" title="Northeast Corridor">\n          Northeast Corridor\n         </a>\n         through\n         <a href="/wiki/Rahway,_New_Jersey" title="Rahway, New Jersey">\n          Rahway, New Jersey\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hudson_bergen_exchange_place.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Hudson_bergen_exchange_place.jpg/220px-Hudson_bergen_exchange_place.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Hudson_bergen_exchange_place.jpg/330px-Hudson_bergen_exchange_place.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Hudson_bergen_exchange_place.jpg/440px-Hudson_bergen_exchange_place.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hudson_bergen_exchange_place.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Two\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hudson-Bergen_Light_Rail" title="Hudson-Bergen Light Rail">\n          Hudson-Bergen Light Rail\n         </a>\n         trains in\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jersey_City" title="Jersey City">\n          Jersey City\n         </a>\n         , New Jersey\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/NJ_Transit" title="NJ Transit">\n        NJ Transit\n       </a>\n       Corporation operates extensive rail and bus service throughout the state. NJ Transit is a state-run corporation that began with the consolidation of several private bus companies in North Jersey. In the early 1980s, it acquired the commuter train operations of\n       <a href="/wiki/Conrail" title="Conrail">\n        Conrail\n       </a>\n       that connect towns in northern and central New Jersey to New York City. NJ Transit has eleven train lines that run throughout different parts of the state. Most of the trains start at various points in the state and most end at either\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Station_(New_York_City)" title="Pennsylvania Station (New York City)">\n        Pennsylvania Station\n       </a>\n       , in New York City, or\n       <a href="/wiki/Hoboken_Terminal" title="Hoboken Terminal">\n        Hoboken Terminal\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Hoboken,_New_Jersey" title="Hoboken, New Jersey">\n        Hoboken\n       </a>\n       . NJ Transit began service between Atlantic City and\n       <a href="/wiki/Lindenwold,_New_Jersey" title="Lindenwold, New Jersey">\n        Lindenwold\n       </a>\n       in 1989 and extended it to\n       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">\n        Philadelphia\n       </a>\n       , Pennsylvania, in the 1990s.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       NJ Transit also operates three\n       <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">\n        light rail\n       </a>\n       systems in the state. The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hudson-Bergen_Light_Rail" title="Hudson-Bergen Light Rail">\n        Hudson-Bergen Light Rail\n       </a>\n       connects\n       <a href="/wiki/Bayonne,_New_Jersey" title="Bayonne, New Jersey">\n        Bayonne\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Bergen,_New_Jersey" title="North Bergen, New Jersey">\n        North Bergen\n       </a>\n       , through\n       <a href="/wiki/Hoboken,_New_Jersey" title="Hoboken, New Jersey">\n        Hoboken\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Jersey_City,_New_Jersey" title="Jersey City, New Jersey">\n        Jersey City\n       </a>\n       with planned expansion into\n       <a href="/wiki/Bergen_County,_New_Jersey" title="Bergen County, New Jersey">\n        Bergen County\n       </a>\n       communities. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Newark_Light_Rail" title="Newark Light Rail">\n        Newark Light Rail\n       </a>\n       is partially underground, and connects downtown Newark with other parts of the city. The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/River_Line_(New_Jersey_Transit)" title="River Line (New Jersey Transit)">\n        River Line\n       </a>\n       connects\n       <a href="/wiki/Trenton,_New_Jersey" title="Trenton, New Jersey">\n        Trenton\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Camden,_New_Jersey" title="Camden, New Jersey">\n        Camden\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port_Authority_Trans-Hudson" title="Port Authority Trans-Hudson">\n        PATH\n       </a>\n       is a subway and above-ground railway which links\n       <a href="/wiki/Hoboken,_New_Jersey" title="Hoboken, New Jersey">\n        Hoboken\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jersey_City,_New_Jersey" title="Jersey City, New Jersey">\n        Jersey City\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Harrison,_New_Jersey" title="Harrison, New Jersey">\n        Harrison\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey" title="Newark, New Jersey">\n        Newark\n       </a>\n       with New York City. The PATH operates four lines that connect various points in North Jersey and New York. The lines all terminate in\n       <a href="/wiki/Hudson_County,_New_Jersey" title="Hudson County, New Jersey">\n        Hudson County\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Essex_County,_New_Jersey" title="Essex County, New Jersey">\n        Essex County\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">\n        Manhattan\n       </a>\n       in New York City.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port_Authority_Transit_Corporation" title="Port Authority Transit Corporation">\n        PATCO\n       </a>\n       High Speedline links\n       <a href="/wiki/Camden_County,_New_Jersey" title="Camden County, New Jersey">\n        Camden County\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">\n        Philadelphia\n       </a>\n       . PATCO operates a single elevated and subway line that runs from\n       <a href="/wiki/Lindenwold,_New_Jersey" title="Lindenwold, New Jersey">\n        Lindenwold\n       </a>\n       to Center City Philadelphia. PATCO operates stations in Lindenwold,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voorhees,_New_Jersey" title="Voorhees, New Jersey">\n        Voorhees\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Cherry_Hill,_New_Jersey" title="Cherry Hill, New Jersey">\n        Cherry Hill\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Haddonfield,_New_Jersey" title="Haddonfield, New Jersey">\n        Haddonfield\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Haddon_Township,_New_Jersey" title="Haddon Township, New Jersey">\n        Haddon Township\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Collingswood,_New_Jersey" title="Collingswood, New Jersey">\n        Collingswood\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Camden,_New_Jersey" title="Camden, New Jersey">\n        Camden\n       </a>\n       , along with four stations in Philadelphia.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">\n        Amtrak\n       </a>\n       also operates numerous long-distance passenger trains in New Jersey to and from neighboring states and around the country. In addition to the Newark Airport connection, other major Amtrak railway stations include\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trenton_(Amtrak_station)" title="Trenton (Amtrak station)">\n        Trenton Rail Station\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropark_(NJT_station)" title="Metropark (NJT station)">\n        Metropark\n       </a>\n       , and the grand historic\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Station_(Newark)" title="Pennsylvania Station (Newark)">\n        Newark Penn Station\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southeastern_Pennsylvania_Transportation_Authority" title="Southeastern Pennsylvania Transportation Authority">\n        SEPTA\n       </a>\n       also has two lines that operate into New Jersey. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Trenton_Line_(SEPTA)" title="Trenton Line (SEPTA)">\n        Trenton Line\n       </a>\n       terminates at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Trenton_Transit_Center" title="Trenton Transit Center">\n        Trenton Transit Center\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Trenton_Line_(SEPTA)" title="West Trenton Line (SEPTA)">\n        West Trenton Line\n       </a>\n       terminates at the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Trenton_Rail_Station" title="West Trenton Rail Station">\n        West Trenton Rail Station\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ewing,_New_Jersey" title="Ewing, New Jersey">\n        Ewing\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/AirTrain_Newark" title="AirTrain Newark">\n        AirTrain Newark\n       </a>\n       is a monorail connecting the Amtrak/NJ Transit station on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Corridor" title="Northeast Corridor">\n        Northeast Corridor\n       </a>\n       to the airport\'s terminals and parking lots.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Some private bus carriers still remain in New Jersey. Most of these carriers operate with state funding to offset losses and state owned buses are provided to these carriers, of which\n       <a href="/wiki/Coach_USA" title="Coach USA">\n        Coach USA\n       </a>\n       companies make up the bulk. Other carriers include private charter and tour bus operators that take gamblers from other parts of New Jersey, New York City,\n       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">\n        Philadelphia\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">\n        Delaware\n       </a>\n       to the casino resorts of Atlantic City.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ferries">\n        Ferries\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MVCapeHenlopen.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1125" data-file-width="1500" height="165"
