//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/MVCapeHenlopen.jpg/440px-MVCapeHenlopen.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MVCapeHenlopen.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_May-Lewes_Ferry" title="Cape May-Lewes Ferry">\n          Cape May-Lewes Ferry\n         </a>\n         connects New Jersey and\n         <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">\n          Delaware\n         </a>\n         across the\n         <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Bay" title="Delaware Bay">\n          Delaware Bay\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In the\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_New_York_and_New_Jersey" title="Port of New York and New Jersey">\n        Port of New York and New Jersey\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/NY_Waterway" title="NY Waterway">\n        New York Waterway\n       </a>\n       has ferry terminals at\n       <a href="/wiki/Belford,_New_Jersey" title="Belford, New Jersey">\n        Belford Harbor\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jersey_City" title="Jersey City">\n        Jersey City\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hoboken,_New_Jersey" title="Hoboken, New Jersey">\n        Hoboken\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weehawken" title="Weehawken">\n        Weehawken\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edgewater_Landing" title="Edgewater Landing">\n        Edgewater Landing\n       </a>\n       . There are\n       <a href="/wiki/Ferry_slip" title="Ferry slip">\n        slips\n       </a>\n       at\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port_Liberte" title="Port Liberte">\n        Port Liberte\n       </a>\n       , Liberty Harbor,\n       <a href="/wiki/Exchange_Place_(Jersey_City)" title="Exchange Place (Jersey City)">\n        Exchange Place\n       </a>\n       in Jersey City,\n       <a href="/wiki/Weehawken_Port_Imperial" title="Weehawken Port Imperial">\n        Port Imperial\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lincoln_Harbor" title="Lincoln Harbor">\n        Lincoln Harbor\n       </a>\n       in Weehawken,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hoboken_Terminal" title="Hoboken Terminal">\n        Hoboken Terminal\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/14th_Street_(Hoboken)" title="14th Street (Hoboken)">\n        14th Street\n       </a>\n       in Hoboken.\n       <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">\n        Manhattan\n       </a>\n       terminals are located at\n       <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">\n        Wall Street\n       </a>\n       /Pier 11,\n       <a href="/wiki/Battery_Park_City_Ferry_Terminal" title="Battery Park City Ferry Terminal">\n        Battery Park City (BPC)\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Midtown_Ferry_Terminal" title="West Midtown Ferry Terminal">\n        West Midtown Ferry Terminal\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Water_Taxi" title="Liberty Water Taxi">\n        Liberty Water Taxi\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jersey_City" title="Jersey City">\n        Jersey City\n       </a>\n       has ferries from\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paulus_Hook" title="Paulus Hook">\n        Paulus Hook\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Liberty_State_Park" title="Liberty State Park">\n        Liberty State Park\n       </a>\n       to (BPC).\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Statue_Cruises" title="Statue Cruises">\n        Statue Cruises\n       </a>\n       has service from Liberty State Park and\n       <a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Liberty_National_Monument" title="Statue of Liberty National Monument">\n        Statue of Liberty National Monument\n       </a>\n       , including\n       <a href="/wiki/Ellis_Island" title="Ellis Island">\n        Ellis Island\n       </a>\n       . (Although there is a bridge from Ellis Island to the park built for renovations on the island it is not open for public use.)\n       <a href="/wiki/SeaStreak" title="SeaStreak">\n        SeaStreak\n       </a>\n       offers services from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Raritan_Bayshore" title="Raritan Bayshore">\n        Raritan Bayshore\n       </a>\n       to Manhattan and during\n       <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">\n        the Met\'s\n       </a>\n       season to\n       <a href="/wiki/Shea_Stadium" title="Shea Stadium">\n        Shea Stadium\n       </a>\n       . The ferries on leave from\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Highlands,_New_Jersey" title="Atlantic Highlands, New Jersey">\n        Atlantic Highlands\n       </a>\n       and two terminals in\n       <a href="/wiki/Highlands,_New_Jersey" title="Highlands, New Jersey">\n        Highlands\n       </a>\n       . Ferry service from\n       <a href="/wiki/Keyport,_New_Jersey" title="Keyport, New Jersey">\n        Keyport\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Perth_Amboy" title="Perth Amboy">\n        Perth Amboy\n       </a>\n       have been also been proposed. Service from\n       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth,_New_Jersey" title="Elizabeth, New Jersey">\n        Elizabeth\n       </a>\n       at\n       <a href="/wiki/Newark_Bay" title="Newark Bay">\n        Newark Bay\n       </a>\n       is proposed in conjunction with re-development plans on the shore near\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jersey_Gardens" title="Jersey Gardens">\n        Jersey Gardens\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">\n        <a href="#cite_note-160">\n         [160]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Bay" title="Delaware Bay">\n        Delaware Bay\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River_and_Bay_Authority" title="Delaware River and Bay Authority">\n        Delaware River and Bay Authority\n       </a>\n       operates the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_May-Lewes_Ferry" title="Cape May-Lewes Ferry">\n        Cape May-Lewes Ferry\n       </a>\n       . The agency also operates the\n       <a href="/wiki/Forts_Ferry_Crossing" title="Forts Ferry Crossing">\n        Forts Ferry Crossing\n       </a>\n       for passengers across the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River" title="Delaware River">\n        Delaware River\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River_Port_Authority" title="Delaware River Port Authority">\n        Delaware River Port Authority\n       </a>\n       operates the\n       <a href="/wiki/RiverLink_Ferry" title="RiverLink Ferry">\n        RiverLink Ferry\n       </a>\n       between the\n       <a href="/wiki/Camden,_New_Jersey" title="Camden, New Jersey">\n        Camden\n       </a>\n       waterfront and\n       <a href="/wiki/Penn%27s_Landing" title="Penn\'s Landing">\n        Penn\'s Landing\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">\n        Philadelphia\n       </a>\n       , Pennsylvania.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Private_bus_carriers">\n        Private bus carriers\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Several private bus lines provide transportation service in the state of New Jersey. Below is a list of major carriers and their areas of operation:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Academy_Bus" title="Academy Bus">\n         Academy\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 commuter bus service from\n        <a href="/wiki/Burlington_County,_New_Jersey" title="Burlington County, New Jersey">\n         Burlington\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Middlesex_County,_New_Jersey" title="Middlesex County, New Jersey">\n         Middlesex\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Monmouth_County,_New_Jersey" title="Monmouth County, New Jersey">\n         Monmouth\n        </a>\n        , and\n        <a href="/wiki/Ocean_County,_New_Jersey" title="Ocean County, New Jersey">\n         Ocean\n        </a>\n        counties to\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wall_Street_(Manhattan)" title="Wall Street (Manhattan)">\n         lower\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Midtown_Manhattan" title="Midtown Manhattan">\n         midtown Manhattan\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Broadway Bus \xe2\x80\x93 local bus service in\n        <a href="/wiki/Bayonne,_New_Jersey" title="Bayonne, New Jersey">\n         Bayonne\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Coach_USA" title="Coach USA">\n         Coach USA\n        </a>\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Community_Coach" title="Community Coach">\n           Community Coach\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 commuter bus service from\n          <a href="/wiki/Essex_County,_New_Jersey" title="Essex County, New Jersey">\n           Essex\n          </a>\n          and\n          <a href="/wiki/Morris_County,_New_Jersey" title="Morris County, New Jersey">\n           Morris\n          </a>\n          counties\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orange_Newark_Elizabeth_Bus" title="Orange Newark Elizabeth </ul>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/DeCamp_Bus_Lines" title="DeCamp Bus Lines">\n         DeCamp Bus Lines\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 commuter bus service from Essex County to Manhattan\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greyhound_Bus" title="Greyhound Bus">\n         Greyhound\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 interstate bus service from terminals in Newark, Atlantic City, and Mount Laurel\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Lakeland_Bus_Lines" title="Lakeland Bus Lines">\n         Lakeland Bus Lines\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 commuter and local bus service from Morris,\n        <a href="/wiki/Somerset_County,_New_Jersey" title="Somerset County, New Jersey">\n         Somerset\n        </a>\n        , Union, and\n        <a href="/wiki/Sussex_County,_New_Jersey" title="Sussex County, New Jersey">\n         Sussex\n        </a>\n        counties to Manhattan\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martz_Trailways" title="Martz Trailways">\n         Martz Trailways\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 service from\n        <a <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Trans-Bridge_Lines" title="Trans-Bridge Lines">\n         Trans-Bridge Lines\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 service from the\n        <a href="/wiki/Skylands_Region" title="Skylands Region">\n         Skylands Region\n        </a>\n        to and from Manhattan\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">\n        Governance\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_New_Jersey" title="Government of New Jersey">\n        Government of New Jersey\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_Jersey" title="Governor of New Jersey">\n        Governor of New Jersey\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_New_Jersey" title="Lieutenant Governor of New Jersey">\n        Lieutenant Governor of New Jersey\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Legislature" title="New Jersey Legislature">\n        New Jersey Legislature\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2006_New_Jersey_State_Government_Shutdown" title="2006 New Jersey State Government Shutdown">\n        2006 New Jersey State Government Shutdown\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chris_Christie_April_2015_(cropped).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2180" data-file-width="1562" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Chris_Christie_April_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Chris_Christie_April_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Chris_Christie_April_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Chris_Christie_April_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Chris_Christie_April_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Chris_Christie_April_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chris_Christie_April_2015_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Chris_Christie" title="Chris Christie">\n          Chris Christie\n         </a>\n         <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">\n          (R)\n         </a>\n         , the\n         <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_New_Jersey" title="List of Governors of New Jersey">\n          55th\n         </a>\n         and current\n         <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_Jersey" title="Governor of New Jersey">\n          Governor of New Jersey\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Executive">\n        Executive\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The position of Governor of New Jersey has been considered one of the most powerful in the nation. Until 2010, the governor was the only statewide elected executive official in the state and appointed numerous government officials. Formerly, an acting governor was even more powerful as he simultaneously served as President of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Jersey_State_Senate" title="New Jersey State Senate">\n        New Jersey State Senate\n       </a>\n       , thus directing half of the legislative and all of the executive process. In 2002 and 2007, President of the State Senate\n       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Codey" title="Richard Codey">\n        Richard Codey\n       </a>\n       held the position of acting governor for a short time, and from 2004 to 2006 Codey became a long-term acting governor due to\n       <a href="/wiki/Jim_McGreevey" title="Jim McGreevey">\n        Jim McGreevey\n       </a>\n       \'s resignation. A 2005 amendment to the state Constitution prevents the Senate President from becoming acting governor in the event of a permanent gubernatorial vacancy without giving up her or his seat in the state Senate.\n       <a href="/wiki/Chris_Christie" title="Chris Christie">\n        Chris Christie\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">\n        Republican\n       </a>\n       ) is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_Jersey" title="Governor of New Jersey">\n        Governor\n       </a>\n       . The governor\'s mansion is\n       <a href="/wiki/Drumthwacket" title="Drumthwacket">\n        Drumthwacket\n       </a>\n       , located in\n       <a href="/wiki/Princeton,_New_Jersey" title="Princeton, New Jersey">\n        Princeton\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Before 2010, New Jersey was one of the few states without a\n       <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_governor_(United_States)" title="Lieutenant governor (United States)">\n        lieutenant governor\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">\n        Republican\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Kim_Guadagno" title="Kim Guadagno">\n        Kim Guadagno\n       </a>\n       was elected the first\n       <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_New_Jersey" title="Lieutenant Governor of New Jersey">\n        Lieutenant Governor of New Jersey\n       </a>\n       and took office on January 19, 2010. She was elected on the Republican ticket with Governor-Elect\n       <a href="/wiki/Chris_Christie" title="Chris Christie">\n        Chris Christie\n       </a>\n       in the November 2009 NJ gubernatorial election. The position was created as the result of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_amendment" title="Constitutional amendment">\n        Constitutional amendment\n       </a>\n       to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Jersey_State_Constitution" title="New Jersey State Constitution">\n        New Jersey State Constitution\n       </a>\n       passed by the voters on November 8, 2005 and effective as of January 17, 2006.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Legislative">\n        Legislative\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Jersey_State_House.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1545" data-file-width="2221" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/New_Jersey_State_House.jpg/220px-New_Jersey_State_House.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/New_Jersey_State_House.jpg/330px-New_Jersey_State_House.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/New_Jersey_State_House.jpg/440px-New_Jersey_State_House.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_Jersey_State_House.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_State_House" title="New Jersey State House">\n          New Jersey State House\n         </a>\n         is topped by its golden dome in\n         <a href="/wiki/Trenton,_New_Jersey" title="Trenton, New Jersey">\n          Trenton\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The current version of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Jersey_State_Constitution" title="New Jersey State Constitution">\n        New Jersey State Constitution\n       </a>\n       was adopted in 1947. It provides for a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicameral" title="Bicameral">\n        bicameral\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Legislature" title="New Jersey Legislature">\n        New Jersey Legislature\n       </a>\n       , consisting of an\n       <a href="/wiki/Upper_house" title="Upper house">\n        upper house\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Senate" title="New Jersey Senate">\n        Senate\n       </a>\n       of 40 members and a\n       <a href="/wiki/Lower_house" title="Lower house">\n        lower house\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_General_Assembly" title="New Jersey General Assembly">\n        General Assembly\n       </a>\n       of 80 members. Each of the 40 legislative districts elects one State Senator and two Assembly members. Assembly members are elected for a two-year term in all odd-numbered years; State Senators are elected in the years ending in 1, 3, and 7 and thus serve either four- or two-year terms.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey is one of only five states that elects its state officials in odd-numbered years. (The others are\n       <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">\n        Kentucky\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">\n        Louisiana\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">\n        Mississippi\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       .) New Jersey holds elections for these offices every four years, in the year following each federal Presidential election year. Thus, the last year when New Jersey elected a Governor was 2013; the next gubernatorial election will occur in 2017, with future gubernatorial elections to take place in 2021, 2025, 2029, etc.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:358px;max-width:358px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:177px;max-width:177px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Robert_Menendez,_official_Senate_photo.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="2368" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Robert_Menendez%2C_official_Senate_photo.jpg/175px-Robert_Menendez%2C_official_Senate_photo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Robert_Menendez%2C_official_Senate_photo.jpg/263px-Robert_Menendez%2C_official_Senate_photo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Robert_Menendez%2C_official_Senate_photo.jpg/350px-Robert_Menendez%2C_official_Senate_photo.jpg 2x" width="175"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          <a href="/wiki/Bob_Menendez" title="Bob Menendez">\n           Robert Menendez\n          </a>\n          <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">\n           (D)\n          </a>\n          , New Jersey\'s current senior\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Senator" title="U.S. Senator">\n           U.S. Senator\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:177px;max-width:177px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cory_Booker,_official_portrait,_114th_Congress.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="825" data-file-width="675" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Cory_Booker%2C_official_portrait%2C_114th_Congress.jpg/175px-Cory_Booker%2C_official_portrait%2C_114th_Congress.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Cory_Booker%2C_official_portrait%2C_114th_Congress.jpg/263px-Cory_Booker%2C_official_portrait%2C_114th_Congress.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Cory_Booker%2C_official_portrait%2C_114th_Congress.jpg/350px-Cory_Booker%2C_official_portrait%2C_114th_Congress.jpg 2x" width="175"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          <a href="/wiki/Cory_Booker" title="Cory Booker">\n           Cory Booker\n          </a>\n          (D), New Jersey\'s current junior U.S. Senator\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div style="clear:left">\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Judicial">\n        Judicial\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_New_Jersey" title="Judiciary of New Jersey">\n        Judiciary of New Jersey\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Supreme_Court" title="New Jersey Supreme Court">\n        New Jersey Supreme Court\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">\n        <a href="#cite_note-161">\n         [161]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       consists of a Chief Justice and six Associate Justices. All are appointed by the Governor with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Advice_and_consent" title="Advice and consent">\n        advice and consent\n       </a>\n       of a majority of the membership of the State Senate. Justices serve an initial seven-year term, after which they can be reappointed to serve until age 70.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Most of the day-to-day work in the New Jersey courts is carried out in the\n       <b>\n        Municipal Courts\n       </b>\n       , where simple traffic tickets, minor criminal offenses, and small civil matters are heard.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       More serious criminal and civil cases are handled by the\n       <b>\n        <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Superior_Court" title="New Jersey Superior Court">\n         Superior Court\n        </a>\n       </b>\n       for each county. All Superior Court judges are appointed by the Governor with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Advice_and_consent" title="Advice and consent">\n        advice and consent\n       </a>\n       of a majority of the membership of the State Senate. Each judge serves an initial seven-year term, after which he or she can be reappointed to serve until age 70. New Jersey\'s judiciary is unusual in that it still has separate courts of law and\n       <a href="/wiki/Equity_(law)" title="Equity (law)">\n        equity\n       </a>\n       , like its neighbor\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">\n        Delaware\n       </a>\n       but unlike most other U.S. states. The\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Superior_Court" title="New Jersey Superior Court">\n        New Jersey Superior Court\n       </a>\n       is divided into Law and Chancery Divisions at the trial level; the Law Division hears both criminal cases and civil lawsuits where the plaintiff\'s primary remedy is\n       <a href="/wiki/Damages" title="Damages">\n        damages\n       </a>\n       , while the Chancery Division hears family cases, civil suits where the plaintiff\'s primary remedy is equitable relief, and probate trials.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Superior Court also has an\n       <b>\n        <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Superior_Court,_Appellate_Division" title="New Jersey Superior Court, Appellate Division">\n         Appellate Division\n        </a>\n       </b>\n       , which functions as the state\'s intermediate\n       <a href="/wiki/Appellate_court" title="Appellate court">\n        appellate court\n       </a>\n       . Superior Court judges are assigned to the Appellate Division by the Chief Justice.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There is also a\n       <b>\n        Tax Court\n       </b>\n       , which is a court of limited jurisdiction. Tax Court judges hear appeals of tax decisions made by County Boards of Taxation. They also hear appeals on decisions made by the Director of the Division of Taxation on such matters as state income, sales and business taxes, and homestead rebates. Appeals from Tax Court decisions are heard in the Appellate Division of Superior Court. Tax Court judges are appointed by the Governor for initial terms of seven years, and upon reappointment are granted tenure until they reach the mandatory retirement age of 70. There are 12 Tax Court judgeships.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Counties">\n        Counties\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_New_Jersey_counties" title="List of New Jersey counties">\n        List of New Jersey counties\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey is divided into 21 counties; 13 date from the colonial era. New Jersey was completely divided into counties by 1692; the present counties were created by dividing the existing ones; most recently\n       <a href="/wiki/Union_County,_New_Jersey" title="Union County, New Jersey">\n        Union County\n       </a>\n       in 1857. New Jersey is the only state in the nation where elected county officials are called "Freeholders," governing each county as part of its own\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Board_of_Chosen_Freeholders" title="Board of Chosen Freeholders">\n        Board of Chosen Freeholders\n       </a>\n       . The number of freeholders in each county is determined by referendum, and must consist of three, five, seven or nine members.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Depending on the county, the executive and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative" title="Legislative">\n        legislative\n       </a>\n       functions may be performed by the Board of Chosen Freeholders or split into separate branches of government. In 16 counties, members of the Board of Chosen Freeholders perform both legislative and executive functions on a commission basis, with each Freeholder assigned responsibility for a department or group of departments. In the other 5 counties (\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_County,_New_Jersey" title="Atlantic County, New Jersey">\n        Atlantic\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bergen_County,_New_Jersey" title="Bergen County, New Jersey">\n        Bergen\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Essex_County,_New_Jersey" title="Essex County, New Jersey">\n        Essex\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hudson_County,_New_Jersey" title="Hudson County, New Jersey">\n        Hudson\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mercer_County,_New_Jersey" title="Mercer County, New Jersey">\n        Mercer\n       </a>\n       ), there is a directly elected\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/County_Executive" title="County Executive">\n        County Executive\n       </a>\n       who performs the executive functions while the Board of Chosen Freeholders retains a legislative and oversight role. In counties without an Executive, a County Administrator (or County Manager) may be hired to perform day-to-day administration of county functions.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Municipalities">\n        Municipalities\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey currently has 565 municipalities; the number was 566 before\n       <a href="/wiki/Princeton_Township,_New_Jersey" title="Princeton Township, New Jersey">\n        Princeton Township\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Princeton_Borough,_New_Jersey" title="Princeton Borough, New Jersey">\n        Princeton Borough\n       </a>\n       merged to form the municipality of\n       <a href="/wiki/Princeton,_New_Jersey" title="Princeton, New Jersey">\n        Princeton\n       </a>\n       on January 1, 2013. Unlike other states, all New Jersey land is part of a municipality. In 2008, Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Jon_Corzine" title="Jon Corzine">\n        Jon Corzine\n       </a>\n       proposed cutting state aid to all towns under 10,000 people, to encourage mergers to reduce administrative costs.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">\n        <a href="#cite_note-162">\n         [162]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In May 2009, the Local Unit Alignment Reorganization and Consolidation Commission began a study of about 40 small communities in South Jersey to decide which ones might be good candidates for consolidation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">\n        <a href="#cite_note-163">\n         [163]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Forms_of_municipal_government">\n        Forms of municipal government\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <table cellpadding="3" cellspacing="0" style="float:right; margin:5px; border:2px solid;">\n       <tr>\n        <td align="left" colspan="2" style="border-bottom:2px solid">\n         <small>\n          <b>\n           <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_New_Jersey" title="Local government in New Jersey">\n            New Jersey municipal government\n           </a>\n          </b>\n         </small>\n         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_New_Jersey.svg" title="Flag of New Jersey">\n          <img alt="Flag of New Jersey" data-file-height="308" data-file-width="512" height="30" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_New_Jersey.svg/50px-Flag_of_New_Jersey.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_New_Jersey.svg/75px-Flag_of_New_Jersey.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_New_Jersey.svg/100px-Flag_of_New_Jersey.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td align="center" colspan="2" style="border-bottom:2px solid; background:#d3d3d3;">\n         <b>\n          Traditional forms\n         </b>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td align="center">\n         <small>\n          <a href="/wiki/Borough_(New_Jersey)" title="Borough (New Jersey)">\n           Borough\n          </a>\n         </small>\n        </td>\n        <td align="center">\n         <small>\n          <a href="/wiki/Township_(New_Jersey)" title="Township (New Jersey)">\n           Township\n          </a>\n         </small>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td align="center" colspan="2">\n         <table border="0">\n          <tr>\n           <td align="center">\n            <small>\n             <a href="/wiki/City_(New_Jersey)" title="City (New Jersey)">\n              City\n             </a>\n            </small>\n           </td>\n           <td align="center" width="100px">\n            <small>\n             <a href="/wiki/Town_(New_Jersey)" title="Town (New Jersey)">\n              Town\n             </a>\n            </small>\n           </td>\n           <td align="center">\n            <small>\n             <a href="/wiki/Village_(New_Jersey)" title="Village (New Jersey)">\n              Village\n             </a>\n            </small>\n           </td>\n          </tr>\n         </table>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td align="center" colspan="2" style="border-top:2px solid; border-bottom:2px solid; background:#d3d3d3;">\n         <b>\n          Modern forms\n         </b>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td align="center" colspan="2">\n         <small>\n          <a href="/wiki/Walsh_Act" title="Walsh Act">\n           Walsh Act commission\n          </a>\n         </small>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td align="center" colspan="2">\n         <small>\n          <a href="/wiki/1923_Municipal_Manager_Law" title="1923 Municipal Manager Law">\n           1923 municipal manager\n          </a>\n         </small>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td align="center" colspan="2" style="border-top:2px solid; border-bottom:2px solid; background:#d3d3d3;">\n         <b>\n          <a href="/wiki/Faulkner_Act" title="Faulkner Act">\n           Faulkner Act\n          </a>\n          forms\n         </b>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td align="center">\n         <small>\n          <a href="/wiki/Faulkner_Act_(mayor%E2%80%93council)" title="Faulkner Act (mayor\xe2\x80\x93council)">\n           Mayor\xe2\x80\x93council\n          </a>\n         </small>\n        </td>\n        <td align="center">\n         <small>\n          <a href="/wiki/Faulkner_Act_(council%E2%80%93manager)" title="Faulkner Act (council\xe2\x80\x93manager)">\n           Council\xe2\x80\x93manager\n          </a>\n         </small>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td align="center" colspan="2">\n         <small>\n          <a href="/wiki/Faulkner_Act_(small_municipality)" title="Faulkner Act (small municipality)">\n           Small municipality\n          </a>\n         </small>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td align="center" colspan="2">\n         <small>\n          <a href="/wiki/Faulkner_Act_(mayor%E2%80%93council%E2%80%93administrator)" title="Faulkner Act (mayor\xe2\x80\x93council\xe2\x80\x93administrator)">\n           Mayor\xe2\x80\x93council\xe2\x80\x93administrator\n          </a>\n         </small>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td align="center" colspan="2" style="border-top:2px solid; border-bottom:2px solid; background:#d3d3d3;">\n         <b>\n          Nonstandard forms\n         </b>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td align="center" colspan="2">\n         <small>\n          <a href="/wiki/Special_charter_(New_Jersey)" title="Special charter (New Jersey)">\n           Special charter\n          </a>\n         </small>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td align="center" colspan="2" style="border-top:2px solid; border-bottom:2px solid; background:#d3d3d3;">\n         <small>\n          <b>\n           Changing form of municipal government\n          </b>\n         </small>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td align="center" colspan="2">\n         <small>\n          <a href="/wiki/Charter_Study_Commission" title="Charter Study Commission">\n           Charter Study Commission\n          </a>\n          <br/>\n         </small>\n         <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar">\n          <small>\n           <span style="word-spacing:0">\n            This box:\n           </span>\n          </small>\n          <ul>\n           <li class="nv-view">\n            <small>\n             <a href="/wiki/Template:NJmunigov" title="Template:NJmunigov">\n              <span title="View this template">\n               view\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </small>\n           </li>\n           <li class="nv-talk">\n            <small>\n             <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:NJmunigov" title="Template talk:NJmunigov">\n              <span title="Discuss this template">\n               talk\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </small>\n           </li>\n           <li class="nv-edit">\n            <small>\n             <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:NJmunigov&amp;action=edit">\n              <span title="Edit this template">\n               edit\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </small>\n           </li>\n          </ul>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Starting in the 20th century, largely driven by reform-minded goals, a series of six modern forms of government was implemented. This began with the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Walsh_Act_(New_Jersey)" title="Walsh Act (New Jersey)">\n        Walsh Act\n       </a>\n       , enacted in 1911 by the\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Legislature" title="New Jersey Legislature">\n        New Jersey Legislature\n       </a>\n       , which provided for a three- or five-member commission elected on a non-partisan basis. This was followed by the\n       <a href="/wiki/1923_Municipal_Manager_Law" title="1923 Municipal Manager Law">\n        1923 Municipal Manager Law\n       </a>\n       , which offered a non-partisan council, provided for a weak mayor elected by and from the members of the council, and introduced a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Council-manager_government" title="Council-manager government">\n        Council-manager government\n       </a>\n       structure with an appointed manager responsible for day-to-day administration of municipal affairs.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faulkner_Act_(New_Jersey)" title="Faulkner Act (New Jersey)">\n        Faulkner Act\n       </a>\n       , originally enacted in 1950 and substantially amended in 1981, offers four basic plans:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faulkner_Act_(Mayor-Council)" title="Faulkner Act (Mayor-Council)">\n        Mayor-Council\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faulkner_Act_(Council-Manager)" title="Faulkner Act (Council-Manager)">\n        Council-Manager\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faulkner_Act_(Small_Municipality)" title="Faulkner Act (Small Municipality)">\n        Small Municipality\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faulkner_Act_(Mayor-Council-Administrator)" title="Faulkner Act (Mayor-Council-Administrator)">\n        Mayor-Council-Administrator\n       </a>\n       . The act provides many choices for communities with a preference for a strong executive and professional management of municipal affairs and offers great flexibility in allowing municipalities to select the characteristics of its government: the number of seats on the Council; seats selected at-large, by wards, or through a combination of both; staggered or concurrent terms of office; and a mayor chosen by the Council or elected directly by voters. Most large municipalities and a majority of New Jersey\'s residents are governed by municipalities with Faulkner Act charters. Municipalities can also formulate their own unique form of government and operate under a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Charter_(New_Jersey)" title="Special Charter (New Jersey)">\n        Special Charter\n       </a>\n       with the approval of the\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Legislature" title="New Jersey Legislature">\n        New Jersey Legislature\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       While municipalities retain their names derived from types of government, they may have changed to one of the modern forms of government, or further in the past to one of the other traditional forms, leading to municipalities with formal names quite baffling to the general public. For example, though there are four municipalities that are officially of the village type,\n       <a href="/wiki/Loch_Arbour,_New_Jersey" title="Loch Arbour, New Jersey">\n        Loch Arbour\n       </a>\n       is the only one remaining with the village form of government. The other three villages \xe2\x80\x93\n       <a href="/wiki/Ridgefield_Park,_New_Jersey" title="Ridgefield Park, New Jersey">\n        Ridgefield Park\n       </a>\n       (now with a Walsh Act form),\n       <a href="/wiki/Ridgewood,_New_Jersey" title="Ridgewood, New Jersey">\n        Ridgewood\n       </a>\n       (now with a Faulkner Act Council-Manager charter) and\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Orange,_New_Jersey" title="South Orange, New Jersey">\n        South Orange\n       </a>\n       (now operates under a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Charter_(New_Jersey)" title="Special Charter (New Jersey)">\n        Special Charter\n       </a>\n       ) \xe2\x80\x93 have all migrated to other non-village forms.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">\n        Politics\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_New_Jersey" title="Politics of New Jersey">\n        Politics of New Jersey\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Social_attitudes_and_issues">\n        Social attitudes and issues\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Socially, New Jersey is considered one of the more\n       <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">\n        liberal\n       </a>\n       states in the nation. Polls indicate that 60% of the population are self-described as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pro-choice" title="Pro-choice">\n        pro-choice\n       </a>\n       , although a majority are opposed to late trimester and\n       <a href="/wiki/Intact_dilation_and_extraction" title="Intact dilation and extraction">\n        intact dilation and extraction\n       </a>\n       and public funding of abortion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">\n        <a href="#cite_note-164">\n         [164]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165">\n        <a href="#cite_note-165">\n         [165]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In a 2009\n       <a href="/wiki/Quinnipiac_University_Polling_Institute" title="Quinnipiac University Polling Institute">\n        Quinnipiac University Polling Institute\n       </a>\n       poll, a plurality supported\n       <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_New_Jersey" title="Same-sex marriage in New Jersey">\n        same-sex marriage\n       </a>\n       49% to 43% opposed,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">\n        <a href="#cite_note-166">\n         [166]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On October 18, 2013, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Supreme_Court" title="New Jersey Supreme Court">\n        New Jersey Supreme Court\n       </a>\n       rendered a provisional, unanimous (7\xe2\x80\x930 vote) order authorizing same-sex marriage in the state, pending a legal appeal by Governor Chris Christie,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167">\n        <a href="#cite_note-167">\n         [167]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       who then withdrew this appeal hours after the inaugural same-sex marriages took place on October 21, 2013.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DroppedAppeal_77-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DroppedAppeal-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_New_Jersey" title="LGBT rights in New Jersey">\n        LGBT rights in New Jersey\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       New Jersey also has some of the most stringent\n       <a href="/wiki/Gun_control" title="Gun control">\n        gun control\n       </a>\n       laws in the U.S. These include bans on assault firearms, hollow-nose bullets and even slingshots. No gun offense in New Jersey is graded less than a felony.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BB_guns" title="BB guns">\n        BB guns\n       </a>\n       and black-powder guns are all treated as modern firearms. New Jersey does not recognize out-of-state gun licenses and aggressively enforces its own gun laws.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">\n        <a href="#cite_note-168">\n         [168]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">\n        Elections\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_New_Jersey" title="Elections in New Jersey">\n        Elections in New Jersey\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_New_Jersey" title="Political party strength in New Jersey">\n        Political party strength in New Jersey\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="float:right; background:#fff3f3;">\n         <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1956" title="United States presidential election, 1956">\n          1956\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td style="text-align:center; background:#fff3f3;">\n         <b>\n          64.68%\n         </b>\n         <i>\n          1,606,942\n         </i>\n        </td>\n        <td style="text-align:center; background:#f0f0ff;">\n         34.23%\n         <i>\n          850,337\n         </i>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="text-align:center; background:#fff3f3;">\n         <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1952" title="United States presidential election, 1952">\n          1952\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td style="text-align:center; background:#fff3f3;">\n         <b>\n          56.81%\n         </b>\n         <i>\n          1,374,613\n         </i>\n        </td>\n        <td style="text-align:center; background:#f0f0ff;">\n         41.99%\n         <i>\n          1,015,902\n         </i>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="text-align:center; background:#fff3f3;">\n         <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1948" title="United States presidential election, 1948">\n          1948\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td style="text-align:center; background:#fff3f3;">\n         <b>\n          50.33%\n         </b>\n         <i>\n          981,124\n         </i>\n        </td>\n        <td style="text-align:center; background:#f0f0ff;">\n         49.96%\n         <i>\n          1,385,415\n         </i>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       In past elections, New Jersey was a\n       <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">\n        Republican\n       </a>\n       bastion, but recently has become a\n       <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">\n        Democratic\n       </a>\n       stronghold. Currently,\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Democratic_State_Committee" title="New Jersey Democratic State Committee">\n        New Jersey Democrats\n       </a>\n       have majority control of both houses of the\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Legislature" title="New Jersey Legislature">\n        New Jersey Legislature\n       </a>\n       (Senate, 24\xe2\x80\x9316, and Assembly, 47\xe2\x80\x9333), a 7\xe2\x80\x935 split of the state\'s twelve seats in the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">\n        U.S. House of Representatives\n       </a>\n       , and both\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">\n        U.S. Senate\n       </a>\n       seats. Although the Democratic Party is very successful statewide, the state had a Republican governor from 1994 to 2002, as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christie_Todd_Whitman" title="Christie Todd Whitman">\n        Christie Todd Whitman\n       </a>\n       won twice with 47% and 49% of the votes, and in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2009_New_Jersey_gubernatorial_election" title="2009 New Jersey gubernatorial election">\n        2009 gubernatorial election\n       </a>\n       , Republican\n       <a href="/wiki/Chris_Christie" title="Chris Christie">\n        Chris Christie\n       </a>\n       defeated incumbent Democrat\n       <a href="/wiki/Jon_Corzine" title="Jon Corzine">\n        Jon Corzine\n       </a>\n       with 48%. In the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2013_New_Jersey_Gubernatorial_election" title="2013 New Jersey Gubernatorial election">\n        2013 gubernatorial election\n       </a>\n       , Christie won reelection with over 60% of the votes. Because each candidate for lieutenant governor runs on the same ticket as the party\'s candidate for governor, the current Governor and Lieutenant Governor are members of the Republican Party. The governor\'s appointments to cabinet and non-cabinet positions may be from either party; for instance, the Attorney General is a Democrat.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In federal elections, the state leans heavily towards the\n       <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">\n        Democratic Party\n       </a>\n       . For many years in the past, however, it was a Republican stronghold, having given comfortable margins of victory to the Republican candidate in the close elections of\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1948" title="United States presidential election, 1948">\n        1948\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1968" title="United States presidential election, 1968">\n        1968\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1976" title="United States presidential election, 1976">\n        1976\n       </a>\n       . New Jersey was a crucial\n       <a href="/wiki/Swing_state" title="Swing state">\n        swing state\n       </a>\n       in the elections of\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1960" title="United States presidential election, 1960">\n        1960\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1968" title="United States presidential election, 1968">\n        1968\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1992" title="United States presidential election, 1992">\n        1992\n       </a>\n       . The last elected Republican to hold a Senate seat from New Jersey was\n       <a href="/wiki/Clifford_P._Case" title="Clifford P. Case">\n        Clifford P. Case\n       </a>\n       in 1979. Newark Mayor\n       <a href="/wiki/Cory_Booker" title="Cory Booker">\n        Cory Booker\n       </a>\n       was elected in October 2013 to join\n       <a href="/wiki/Bob_Menendez" title="Bob Menendez">\n        Robert Menendez\n       </a>\n       to make New Jersey the first state with concurrent serving black and Latino U.S. senators.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">\n        <a href="#cite_note-170">\n         [170]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The state\'s Democratic strongholds include\n       <a href="/wiki/Camden_County,_New_Jersey" title="Camden County, New Jersey">\n        Camden County\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Essex_County,_New_Jersey" title="Essex County, New Jersey">\n        Essex County\n       </a>\n       (typically the state\'s most Democratic county\xe2\x80\x94it includes\n       <a href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey" title="Newark, New Jersey">\n        Newark\n       </a>\n       , the state\'s largest city),\n       <a href="/wiki/Hudson_County,_New_Jersey" title="Hudson County, New Jersey">\n        Hudson County\n       </a>\n       (the second-strongest Democratic county, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Jersey_City,_New_Jersey" title="Jersey City, New Jersey">\n        Jersey City\n       </a>\n       , the state\'s second-largest city);\n       <a href="/wiki/Mercer_County,_New_Jersey" title="Mercer County, New Jersey">\n        Mercer County\n       </a>\n       (especially around\n       <a href="/wiki/Trenton,_New_Jersey" title="Trenton, New Jersey">\n        Trenton\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Princeton,_New_Jersey" title="Princeton, New Jersey">\n        Princeton\n       </a>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/Middlesex_County,_New_Jersey" title="Middlesex County, New Jersey">\n        Middlesex County\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Union_County,_New_Jersey" title="Union County, New Jersey">\n        Union County\n       </a>\n       (including\n       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth,_New_Jersey" title="Elizabeth, New Jersey">\n        Elizabeth\n       </a>\n       , the state\'s fourth-largest city).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171">\n        <a href="#cite_note-171">\n         [171]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The suburban northwestern and southeastern counties of the state are reliably Republican: Republicans have support along the coast in\n       <a href="/wiki/Ocean_County,_New_Jersey" title="Ocean County, New Jersey">\n        Ocean County\n       </a>\n       and in the mountainous northwestern part of the state, especially\n       <a href="/wiki/Morris_County,_New_Jersey" title="Morris County, New Jersey">\n        Morris County\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Sussex_County,_New_Jersey" title="Sussex County, New Jersey">\n        Sussex County\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Warren_County,_New_Jersey" title="Warren County, New Jersey">\n        Warren County\n       </a>\n       . Other suburban counties, especially\n       <a href="/wiki/Bergen_County,_New_Jersey" title="Bergen County, New Jersey">\n        Bergen County\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Burlington_County,_New_Jersey" title="Burlington County, New Jersey">\n        Burlington County\n       </a>\n       had the majority of votes go to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">\n        Democratic Party\n       </a>\n       . In the 2008 election, President\n       <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">\n        Barack Obama\n       </a>\n       won New Jersey with approximately fifty-seven percent of the vote, compared to\n       <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">\n        McCain\'s\n       </a>\n       forty-one percent. Independent candidate\n       <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Nader" title="Ralph Nader">\n        Ralph Nader\n       </a>\n       garnered less than one percent of the vote.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       About one-third of the state\'s counties are considered "swing" counties, but some go more one way than others. For example,\n       <a href="/wiki/Salem_County,_New_Jersey" title="Salem County, New Jersey">\n        Salem County\n       </a>\n       , the same is true with\n       <a href="/wiki/Passaic_County,_New_Jersey" title="Passaic County, New Jersey">\n        Passaic County\n       </a>\n       , with a highly populated Hispanic Democratic south (including\n       <a href="/wiki/Paterson,_New_Jersey" title="Paterson, New Jersey">\n        Paterson\n       </a>\n       , the state\'s third-largest city) and a rural, Republican north; with the "swing" township of\n       <a href="/wiki/Wayne,_New_Jersey" title="Wayne, New Jersey">\n        Wayne\n       </a>\n       in the middle. Other "swing" counties like\n       <a href="/wiki/Monmouth_County,_New_Jersey" title="Monmouth County, New Jersey">\n        Monmouth County\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Somerset_County,_New_Jersey" title="Somerset County, New Jersey">\n        Somerset County\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_May_County,_New_Jersey" title="Cape May County, New Jersey">\n        Cape May County\n       </a>\n       tend to go Republican, as they also have population in conservative areas, although Somerset has recently trended Democratic.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       To be eligible to vote in a U.S. election, all New Jerseyans are required to start their residency in the state 30 days prior to an election and register 21 days prior to election day.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172">\n        <a href="#cite_note-172">\n         [172]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Capital_punishment">\n        Capital punishment\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment_in_New_Jersey" title="Capital punishment in New Jersey">\n        Capital punishment in New Jersey\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       On December 17, 2007, Governor Jon Corzine signed into law a bill that would eliminate the death penalty in New Jersey. New Jersey is the first state to pass such legislation since\n       <a href="/wiki/Iowa" title="Iowa">\n        Iowa\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">\n        West Virginia\n       </a>\n       eliminated executions in 1965.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173">\n        <a href="#cite_note-173">\n         [173]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Corzine also signed a bill that would downgrade the Death Row prisoners\' sentences from "Death" to "Life in Prison with No Parole."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174">\n        <a href="#cite_note-174">\n         [174]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Points_of_interest">\n        Points of interest\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">\n        Museums\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable"        </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Entertainment_and_concert_venues">\n        Entertainment and concert venues\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image"     </a>\n         from the Mariner\'s Landing Ferris wheel at night\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Visitors and residents take advantage of and contribute to performances at the numerous music, theater, and dance companies and venues located throughout the state, including:\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n id="Theme_parks">\n        Theme parks\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:center; max-width:908px;">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="">\n        <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">\n         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SFGadv_Skyline.jpg" title="Skyline of Six Flags Great Adventure in Jackson Township, Ocean County, the world\'s largest theme park as of 2013. To the far left is Kingda Ka, the world\'s tallest roller coaster.">\n          <img alt="" data-file-height="989" data-file-width="6392" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/SFGadv_Skyline.jpg/900px-SFGadv_Skyline.jpg" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/SFGadv_Skyline.jpg/1800px-SFGadv_Skyline.jpg 2x" width="900"/>\n         </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a href="/wiki/File:SFGadv_Skyline.jpg" title="File:SFGadv Skyline.jpg">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Skyline of\n         <a href="/wiki/Six_Flags_Great_Adventure" title="Six Flags Great Adventure">\n          Six Flags Great Adventure\n         </a>\n         in\n         <a href="/wiki/Jackson_Township,_New_Jersey" title="Jackson Township, New Jersey">\n          Jackson Township\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Ocean_County,_New_Jersey" title="Ocean County, New Jersey">\n          Ocean County\n         </a>\n         , the world\'s largest\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theme_park" title="Theme park">\n          theme park\n         </a>\n         as of 2013.\n    .\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176">\n          <a href="#cite_note-176">\n           [176]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n
